# Couch Heroes: Executive & Senior Compensation Strategy  
Pre-revenue AA studio with teams in the UK (London-weighted) and Greece (Athens-weighted)

## Summary
You’re hiring and retaining C-level and senior leaders across two very different labour markets. The plan below sets a clear, stage-appropriate pay philosophy, codifies how we handle UK vs Greece location effects, and provides role-specific cash benchmarks with four-quartile bands plus recommended bonus targets. Where reliable, recent market data exists for games, I use it. Where the data is thinner (especially Greece and game-specific exec roles), I triangulate from reputable national salary guides and games-adjacent reports, and I label those inferences. Sources are cited inline.

---

## 1) Compensation philosophy for a pre-revenue AA studio
1) **Cash lean, equity forward.** Bias base salaries to Q2–Q3 locally, keep target cash bonuses modest and milestone-anchored, and use equity to close senior gaps. Index Ventures’ Europe guidance remains the best public reference for early-stage equity norms. citeturn4search0turn4search3turn4search18  
2) **Local-market anchoring.** Set bands per location rather than using a single global rate. For London, anchor to London medians. For Athens, anchor to Greek executive tech bands. Randstad Greece publishes monthly bands (expressed on a 14-salary basis), which we convert to annual for comparability. citeturn0search4turn1search4  
3) **Simple, transparent structure.** Each role gets four quartiles for base pay (Q1 low to Q4 high), a **target bonus range** suitable for pre-revenue AA, and an indicative **Target Total Cash (TTC)** by applying the mid-point bonus to each quartile.  
4) **Stage-correct variable pay.** Use binary or tiered milestones (funding closed, vertical slice, content gate, soft-launch KPI gates) rather than revenue multipliers until the game is commercial.

---

## 4) Equity guidance (grant size at pre-revenue, standard 4-year vest, 1-year cliff)
*Benchmarks in Europe vary and exact role-by-stage tables are often gated; use these as practical, Europe-appropriate ranges and adjust for founders vs hired execs.* References: Index Ventures “Rewarding Talent” and toolset. citeturn4search0turn4search9

| Role | Typical early-stage equity range |
|---|---|
| CEO (hired, not founder) | 1.0–3.0% FD on hire |
| COO | 0.5–1.5% |
| CTO | 0.5–2.0% |
| CFO | 0.25–1.0% |
| Executive Producer / Head of Production | 0.10–0.50% |

**Location parity:** Equity should not vary by country. Keep one global policy and communicate that equity equalises long-run outcomes across markets.

---

## 5) Benefits and statutory differences to plan for
**UK (London):** Private medical and dental, employer pension contribution, life assurance, 25+ days holiday plus bank holidays, EMI options where eligible. For salary context, multiple UK guides confirm London premiums for senior roles. citeturn2search12turn2search3  
**Greece (Athens):** 13th and 14th salaries are standard in calculations used by Randstad; top up with private medical, meal benefits, and remote/hybrid stipends as needed. Ensure option scheme is compliant with current Greek tax treatment of options. citeturn1search4

---

## 6) How to use these bands in offers
1) **Pick the right quartile.**  
   • Scarce, must-have hire or turnaround need: Q3–Q4 base locally, nearer the top of the bonus range, equity at the upper end.  
   • Strong but not rare: Q2 base, mid bonus, mid equity.  
   • Founder-CEO: Q1–Q2 cash plus above-table founder equity.

2) **Tie variable pay to milestones, not revenue.** For example: 25% annual target paid in tranches on (a) funding close, (b) vertical slice exit criteria, (c) first platform greenlight, (d) soft-launch KPI gate.

3) **Avoid cross-border resentment.** Publish the London and Athens bands internally. State that equity, titles, and progression are location-agnostic.

---

## 7) Ready-to-issue package examples
These use the recommended target bonus mid-points and sit at Q2 unless noted.

- **UK Executive Producer (London):** £78k base, 15% target bonus, TTC £89.7k, equity 0.20–0.35%, private medical, 6% employer pension. citeturn0search5  
- **UK CFO (London), strong hire:** Q3 base £306k, 30% target bonus, TTC ~£397.8k, equity 0.4–0.7%. citeturn2search14  
- **Greece CTO (Athens):** €140k base, 20% target bonus, TTC €168k, equity 0.7–1.2%, private medical top-up. citeturn0search4  
- **Greece COO (Athens), mid-market:** €98.5k base, 25% target bonus, TTC €123.1k, equity 0.4–0.8%. citeturn3search2

---

## Evidence notes and caveats
- UK EP numbers: Glassdoor has good coverage; a 2025 immersive/gaming survey shows London EP clustering around £70–95k, which aligns with Q2–low Q3 here. citeturn0search5turn2search13  
- London CTO/CFO/COO: Morgan McKinley, Robert Half, Robert Walters, and Glassdoor provide overlapping ranges; I used those for quartiles and sanity checks. citeturn0search18turn2search14turn2search12turn3search4  
- Greece exec roles: Randstad’s tech bands (monthly on a 14-salary basis) plus SalaryExpert and Glassdoor for CFO/COO. EP is inferred from CPO/Product Director bands because Greek games-specific EP data is sparse. citeturn0search4turn1search7turn1search10turn3search2  
- Equity: Use Index Ventures “Rewarding Talent” as the European reference point; adapt for founder vs hired execs. citeturn4search0

---

## Decision guidance
- **Default offers:** Q2 base, mid bonus, mid equity.  
- **Stretch hires:** Move to Q3 base and top-quartile equity before raising cash bonuses.  
- **Founder pay:** Keep conservative until revenue or financing inflects.

# Restating your brief

# Style changes I will apply

# Sample rewrite slice

## 1) What this compensation plan is and how to use it
This plan sets four cash bands for each executive role in London and Athens. Each band shows base pay and a target bonus so you can see Target Total Cash at a glance. Use Q1 when cash is tight or the candidate has gaps. Use Q2 as the default for strong hires. Move to Q3 or Q4 only when the role is scarce, the impact is critical, or you need to close a competitive offer. Equity does not vary by location. It is the primary long-term equaliser between London and Athens.

## 2) How we handle two very different markets
London and Athens have different labour costs and statutory norms. We anchor pay locally, publish both sets of bands internally, and explain the logic. We avoid resentment by keeping titles, progression rules, and equity identical in both locations. Variable pay is tied to stage-appropriate milestones, not revenue, until the game is commercial.

## 3) Example role, rewritten for clarity
### Executive Producer
**Role intent.** Owns production outcomes from vertical slice to launch and Live Ops readiness. Directs schedules, budgets, cross-discipline delivery, and risk.

**Cash structure.** Target bonus 10–25 percent. Recommend 15 percent as default at pre-revenue.

**Quartiles.**  
London  
- Q1: £56k base. TTC about £64k at 15 percent.  
- Q2: £78k base. TTC about £90k at 15 percent.  
- Q3: £113k base. TTC about £130k at 15 percent.  
- Q4: £163k base. TTC about £188k at 15 percent.

Athens  
- Q1: €53.2k base. TTC about €61.2k at 15 percent.  
- Q2: €62.0k base. TTC about €71.3k at 15 percent.  
- Q3: €69.8k base. TTC about €80.3k at 15 percent.  
- Q4: €72.8k base. TTC about €83.7k at 15 percent.

**Equity guidance.** 0.10–0.50 percent with a four-year vest and one-year cliff. Do not vary by location.

**Offer rule of thumb.** Default to Q2 cash, 15 percent target bonus, and mid-band equity. Move to Q3 only when the candidate is scarce or you need speed to a critical milestone.

## 4) Milestones that release bonus for pre-revenue
- Funding milestone agreed with the Board.  
- Vertical slice exit criteria met and accepted.  
- First platform greenlight achieved.  
- Soft-launch KPI gate met on retention and stability.

Alright Glen — here’s a clear, multi-page brief written as an HR/comp analyst for a games studio. I’ll restate what you asked for, explain the logic, then give location-specific ranges for Chief, VP and Director roles in London (UK) and Athens (Greece). I’ve kept the tone plain and direct, and I’ve used current market sources so leadership can defend these numbers.

# Couch Heroes Executive & Senior Leadership Pay Guide  
Prepared by: Salary Analyst & HR Lead, Games Industry  
Date: 27 October 2025 (Europe/London)

## 1) What you asked for and how to use this guide
You want a practical way to set total cash compensation for Chiefs, VPs and Directors at a pre-revenue AA studio operating in two markets: London and Athens. Total cash here means base salary plus annual bonus targets. Because Greece commonly uses 13th/14th salary payments, I call that out so we compare on an annualised basis. Ranges are shown in four quartiles so you can place an offer at the low end (Q1) through top-of-market (Q4), and I’ve given short notes on when to hire into each quartile.

## 2) Pay philosophy for a pre-revenue AA studio
1) Pay competitively enough to hire bar-raising leaders without outspending AAA.  
2) Bias cash to roles that are critical path for shipping the game or raising capital.  
3) Use consistent bonus targets by level so total cash is predictable and performance-linked.  
4) Keep location policy explicit: London ranges reflect UK market rates; Athens ranges reflect Greek market rates and the local pay structure.

## 3) Method and sources (in brief)
I triangulated recent UK market guides and crowd-sourced datasets for London, and ERI/SalaryExpert plus reputable payroll explainers for Greece. When a source gave total pay percentiles, I translated those into quartiles. If only a range was published, I set Q2 near midpoint and Q4 near 90th-percentile guidance, stating assumptions in the notes. Key London executive benchmarks come from Glassdoor percentiles for CEO and COO, and CFO ranges from Robert Walters and Morgan McKinley; London CTO from recent market data; games-specific London production leadership from TechNET Immersive’s 2025 gaming salary survey. Greek executive and director benchmarks are from ERI/SalaryExpert pages, which publish Athens-specific averages and ranges. See citations in-line where figures are referenced. citeturn3search0turn24view0turn16search1turn16search0turn18view0turn14search10turn13view0

## 4) How to read the tables
• Currency: UK in GBP, Greece in EUR.  
• Each table shows Base Salary quartiles (Q1 low, Q2 mid, Q3 high, Q4 top of market) and a typical Bonus Target for that role.  
• On-target total cash (OTC) = Base × (1 + Bonus%). Example: £140k base with 25% target bonus ⇒ £175k OTC.  
• Band placement rules:  
  – Q1: early stage, scope still forming, or candidate stretching into the seat.  
  – Q2: solid fit, typical experience for a pre-revenue AA studio.  
  – Q3: high performer with proven AA/AAA track record or scarce skill.  
  – Q4: top-tier hire, strong big-studio pedigree, or pivotal fund-raising mandate.

---

## 6) Greece (Athens) — Chiefs, VPs, Directors

Important local structure: Greek law provides Christmas, Easter and summer holiday allowances that together equal roughly two additional months of pay each year. Employers either pay these as separate allowances (13th/14th month) or absorb them into a 12-month quoted salary. The tables below show annualised figures so you can compare apples to apples with the UK. citeturn23search1turn23search2turn23search8

| Director of Production | €60k | €75k | €90k | €100k–€110k | 10–15% | Calibrated from Greek director-level engineering plus Athens senior production premiums. |
| Director of Marketing | €90k | €110k–€115k | €125k | €135k | 10–15% | Athens Marketing Director avg ~€113k. citeturn3search15 |

Notes on Greece: If you quote a 12-month salary, state clearly whether the Christmas/Easter/holiday allowances are included or paid in addition. Many multinationals embed them in the annual figure for simplicity, but payroll must still pay them in the required months. citeturn23search1turn23search9

---

## 7) Benefits and allowances to standardise by location
United Kingdom  
• Pension: auto-enrolment with employer contribution that keeps you competitive in tech (often 4–8%).  
• Private medical and dental for leadership.  
• Life assurance 3–4× salary.  
• Season ticket or cycle-to-work only if you want to mirror market norms.  
• Holiday 25–28 days plus bank holidays.

Greece  
• Employer social contributions are materially higher than the UK; model total employer cost separately from salary.  
• 13th/14th month payments as above.  
• Private medical is a differentiator for senior hires.  
• Holiday allowance must be paid per Greek rules when not embedded. citeturn23search2

---

## 8) Equity: not cash, but do not ignore it
You asked for total cash, but for senior hires at a pre-revenue AA aiming for AAA, small option grants or RSUs help offset taking Q2 cash instead of Q3. Typical tech-adjacent practice:  
• Chiefs: 0.3–1.0% depending on dilution plan and stage.  
• VPs: 0.1–0.4%.  
• Directors: 0.02–0.1%.  
Cliff and vesting: 1-year cliff, 4-year vest. Refreshers tied to performance milestones.

---

## 9) Offer governance
• Pick the location band first. Do not “average” Athens and London.  
• Decide your default quartile by level: for Chiefs, default Q2–Q3; for VPs Q2; for Directors Q2.  
• Only use Q4 for one of: closing a unicorn candidate, proven AAA pedigree, or the role directly unlocks funding.  
• Always state both Base and OTC in the offer, and in Greece clarify if the 13th/14th are included in the annual figure.  
• Review ranges every 6 months while pre-revenue; lock them for 12 months post-fundraise.

---

## 10) Why these numbers hold up
• London CEO and COO quartiles reflect current 25th/50th/75th/90th percentiles for total pay in Oct 2025. citeturn3search0turn24view0  
• London CFO ranges are consistent across multiple 2025 guides and percentile data. citeturn16search1turn16search16  
• London VP Engineering percentiles are current to Oct 2025. citeturn3search5  
• Games-specific London production leadership ranges are from TechNET Immersive’s 2025 gaming survey. citeturn18view0  
• Athens exec and director levels come from ERI/SalaryExpert Athens pages that list average and range for each role. citeturn14search10turn14search5turn13view0turn1search0  
• The Greek 13th/14th salary structure and payment timing are confirmed by the Ministry of Labour and several current payroll guides. citeturn23search1turn23search2turn23search8

---

# Couch Heroes Leadership Compensation Guide  
Prepared by: Compensation Analyst & HR Lead, Games Industry  
Date: 27 Oct 2025

## 1) Purpose and how to use this guide
This guide sets four **cash quartiles** for Chief, VP and Director roles in **London (UK)** and **Athens (Greece)**. Each role shows base pay by quartile, a **target bonus** range suitable for a pre-revenue AA studio, and short notes explaining the logic. Use Q2 as your default for solid hires; move to Q3–Q4 only for scarce talent or critical milestones. UK and Greece bands are **location-anchored**; **equity is location-agnostic**.

## 2) Data sources and validity
- **UK games roles**: TechNET Immersive & Gaming 2025 (role bands and London uplift) and Skillsearch 2024/25 (industry-wide view). These are the core sources for Production and Creative leadership. citeturn0search0turn0search1  
- **Greece executive roles**: ERI/SalaryExpert Athens pages for CEO/President/CTO; these are employer- and employee-reported survey datasets with 2025 currency. Statutory allowances and employer cost treatment follow the 2025 Greece Payroll Guide. citeturn0search4turn0search9turn0search15turn1search11

## 3) Location policy
- **Cash**: priced to the **local market** (London vs Athens).  
- **Equity**: the same policy globally to equalise long-run outcomes.  
- **Greece**: Clarify whether annual offers **embed** the 13th/14th salary or pay them separately; the payroll and employee experience differ. citeturn1search11

## 4) Quartiles and bonus definitions
- **Quartiles**: Q1 (entry/early stage), Q2 (default), Q3 (scarce/impactful), Q4 (top of market).  
- **On-target cash (OTC)**: Base × (1 + target bonus%).  
- **Pre-revenue AA**: bonuses are **milestone** based (funding, vertical slice exit, platform greenlight, soft-launch KPI gate), not revenue multipliers.

## 5) Worked examples (starter slice)

### 5.1 UK — Executive Producer (London)  
**Sources**: TechNET Immersive & Gaming 2025 lists Lead/Executive Producer at **£70k–£95k in London**. We convert that published range into quartile bands to aid offer placement. citeturn0search0

- **Target bonus (AA, pre-rev)**: 10–20% (recommend 15%).  
- **Quartile bands (base, London):**  
  - Q1: **£70k–£76k**  
  - Q2: **£76k–£83k**  
  - Q3: **£83k–£89k**  
  - Q4: **£89k–£95k**  
- **Why these elements**: TechNET gives the current London band; quartiling that band makes offers consistent and defensible. Bonus targets are kept modest at pre-revenue so cash burn stays aligned with stage.

### 5.2 Greece — Chief Executive (Athens)  
**Sources**: ERI/SalaryExpert shows **Greece CEO** average around **€211k**, with experience-based range roughly **€128k (entry)** to **€354k (senior)**; Athens often sits near or above national average. We quartile the ERI range for Athens and state the Greece payroll handling. citeturn0search4

- **Target bonus (AA, pre-rev)**: 20–30% (recommend 25%).  
- **Quartile bands (base, Athens):**  
  - Q1: **€128k–€185k**  
  - Q2: **€185k–€241k**  
  - Q3: **€241k–€298k**  
  - Q4: **€298k–€354k**  
- **Why these elements**: Greece lacks games-specific C-suite data; ERI provides a current national/Athens executive range, which we quartile for structured offers. We will show in the appendix whether your offers **embed** or **separately pay** the 13th/14th month to avoid confusion in OTC and employer on-costs. citeturn1search11

*(In the full build, I’ll produce the same tables for CEO/COO/CTO/CFO/CPO, plus VP and Director tracks, for both locations. UK Production and Creative will lean on TechNET and Skillsearch; Greek C-suite will lean on ERI with clear notes where the data is tech-adjacent rather than games-only.)*

## 6) Benefits and on-cost notes (short)
- **UK**: private medical and dental for leadership, life assurance, employer pension contribution, 25–28 holidays plus bank holidays.  
- **Greece**: higher employer social contributions and 13th/14th month handling; private medical is a differentiator at seniority. Use the payroll guide to model employer cost vs cash shown to the employee. citeturn1search11

## 7) Offer governance
1) Choose the **location band** first.  
2) Default to **Q2**; move to Q3 or Q4 only for scarcity or milestone urgency.  
3) State **Base, Bonus target, OTC**, and for Greece, state clearly how 13th/14th is handled.  
4) Review ranges every 6 months while pre-revenue; lock for 12 months post-funding.

## How to use these bands
• Stage fit: for a pre-revenue AA studio, start offers in Q1–Q2. Reserve Q3–Q4 for exceptional candidates, competing offers, or scarce profiles.  
• UK vs Greece: compare total compensation, not base alone. If 13th/14th salaries apply in Greece, either embed them into the quoted annual gross or show them as explicit allowances alongside base for clarity. citeturn5search1  
• Refresh cadence: review annually against current guides. UK merit budgets this year are generally mid-single-digit as a planning anchor. citeturn20search14

## Variable pay and equity (policy guidance)
**Bonuses**  
• Directors/VPs: set 15–35% target STI pre-revenue, bias to the lower end until cashflow improves.  
• C-suite: set 25–50% target STI pre-revenue, with a hard cap and a strong deferral or equity-settlement option. Market data shows high leverage is common at larger caps, but that is not suitable for a pre-revenue studio. citeturn20search10turn20search2

**Equity**  
Suggested planning ranges for a pre-revenue AA studio targeting EMI in the UK and standard options in Greece:  
• CEO / Head of Studio: 1.0%–3.0% options  
• CTO / COO / CFO: 0.3%–1.0%  
• VPs: 0.1%–0.4%  
• Directors: 0.05%–0.20%

These ranges align with European practice where executives often receive a larger share of the pool relative to the US; calibrate to pool size, dilution plan and role criticality. Use EMI where eligible in the UK. citeturn19search14

# Couch Heroes Executive & Senior Leadership Compensation Guide 2025  
AA studio, pre-revenue, with locations in London, UK and Athens, Greece

Set fair, defensible Total Cash Compensation (base salary + target bonus) bands for Chief, VP and Director roles, with clear guidance for offers across both locations and at pre-revenue stage. This document is explanatory, practical, and specific to a games studio operating in the UK and Greece.

### Method recap

# Executive summary
Couch Heroes is setting leadership pay for a pre-revenue AA studio with teams in London and Athens. The goal is to hire and retain Chiefs, VPs, and Directors with clear, defensible total-cash bands by location, plus straightforward rules for when to use each quartile.

What changes with this guide  
- Separate, location-anchored bands for London and Athens.  
- Four quartiles per role that map cleanly to hiring situations.  
- Target bonus ranges that fit a pre-revenue stage, paid on milestones rather than revenue.  
- Equity policy that is identical across locations.

Why this now  
- Recruiting is active. Offers must be consistent and explainable.  
- UK and Greece have different labour markets and payroll norms. Using one global rate creates pay friction.  
- Pre-revenue cash should favour Q1–Q2 with equity balancing the long term.

How to use it  
- Choose the location band first.  
- Start at Q2 for solid hires. Use Q3 only for scarce talent or critical milestones.  
- Always state base, target bonus, and on-target cash. In Greece, state whether Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are included in the annual figure or paid separately.

# The pay model in one page
Definitions  
- Total cash means base salary plus target annual bonus.  
- Quartiles are derived from current 2025 ranges. Q1 is the lower quarter, Q4 is top of market for the role and location.  
- Equity is outside total cash and does not vary by location.

Bonus policy at pre-revenue  
- Directors and VPs: 10 to 25 percent target.  
- C-suite: 20 to 40 percent target.  
- Payouts tied to agreed milestones such as funding close, vertical slice exit, first platform greenlight, and soft-launch KPI gate.

# Couch Heroes Leadership Compensation White Paper 2025  
AA, pre-revenue. Locations: London, UK and Athens, Greece.

## Executive summary
Couch Heroes needs a clear, location-anchored pay architecture that can hire and retain senior leaders before revenue. This paper sets the rules for base pay, bonus, and equity by level and location, explains how to place offers in quartiles, and defines the governance that keeps decisions consistent. The ranges are games-relevant in the UK and defensible in Greece where games-specific executive data are sparse.

### Decisions
- Use two location anchors: London for UK, Athens for Greece. Offers are set in local currency.
- Place most pre-revenue offers in Q1 or Q2. Use Q3 for scarce profiles. Use Q4 only with CEO and board approval.
- Bonuses are milestone-driven at pre-revenue. Equity is location-agnostic and sized by level and impact.
- Greece follows the local practice of Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances. When comparing across locations, annualise correctly.

### What changes for hiring managers
- One page per role family with the band, the default quartile for pre-revenue, and the target bonus range.
- A simple offer script and a checklist that forces location choice, quartile justification, and governance sign-off.

---

## 1. Objectives and scope
- Build a defensible total-cash structure for Chief, VP, and Director roles that matches an AA studio aiming for AAA standards.
- Make London and Athens offers truly comparable after accounting for local pay norms and allowances.
- Keep the system simple to operate, but strict enough to protect parity and budget.

**In scope:** CEO, CFO, COO, CTO, CPO or Head of Production; VP Engineering, VP Production, VP Marketing, VP Creative; Director of Engineering, Director of Production, Marketing Director, Executive Producer.  
**Out of scope:** IC roles and non-leadership bands.

---

## 2. Compensation philosophy
- **Market-anchored, location-specific:** set base pay at the local market for the role. Do not convert one location’s cash to the other when issuing offers.
- **Stage-appropriate:** pre-revenue uses lower cash within band, modest bonus targets, and meaningful equity.
- **Role clarity and parity:** titles map to scope and outcomes. Similar roles sit in similar quartiles unless the business case shows otherwise.
- **Equity as the long-term equaliser:** equity policy is location-agnostic and tied to level, impact, and cliff/vesting rules.

---

## 3. Data, method, and data quality notes
- **Sources:** UK games leadership from current 2025 games surveys for production and studio roles. UK executive tech and finance roles from 2025 London guides. Greece from reputable Athens and Greece-wide executive datasets where games samples are thin.  
- **Quartiles:** where a source provides a min–max range, quartiles are even splits to create Q1–Q4 boundaries.  
- **Currency:** offers are issued in local currency. For cross-location discussion, show both local figures and a single date FX snapshot.  
- **Greek allowances:** private sector typically pays Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances. Annualise correctly for budget and clarity in offers.

Governance requires that the Evidence Table in Appendix E is maintained and dated.

---

## 4. Role architecture and levelling
- **Chiefs:** company-wide outcomes, budget or P&L responsibility, direct reports include VPs and Directors, accountable for platform, funding, or studio performance.  
- **VPs:** functional strategy, cross-team execution, accountable for delivery and discipline health.  
- **Directors:** discipline leadership, team throughput, quality bars, and schedule adherence.

Hiring triggers and promotion signals appear per role family in Appendix C.

---

## 5. Pay architecture

### 5.1 Base pay bands
- **London, UK:** games-specific bands for production and studio leadership. Cross-industry executive bands for CTO, CFO, COO, and Marketing Director where games samples are limited.  
- **Athens, Greece:** Athens or Greece-wide executive bands for Chiefs and functional leadership. Where games data are thin, we use executive market references and state that fact.

The full band tables by role and location are in Appendix A. They show Q1 to Q4 for base pay and the typical target bonus range.

### 5.2 Bonus policy at pre-revenue
- **Targets:** Directors and VPs 10–25 percent. Chiefs 20–40 percent.  
- **Design:** simple, auditable goals. Payout at quarter-end after evidence review.  
- **Milestones to choose from:** platform vertical slice exit, online services stable at target CCU and crash rate, first-party submission readiness, soft-launch KPI gate, first funding tranche close, build pipeline stability.  
- **Deferral:** chief payouts above 100 percent of target can be partially deferred or settled in equity subject to board approval.  
- **Clawback:** for material misstatement or misconduct.

### 5.3 Equity policy (location-agnostic)
- CEO: 1.5 to 3.0 percent at grant, four-year vest, one-year cliff, standard leaver rules.  
- CTO, COO, CFO: 0.3 to 1.0 percent.  
- VPs: 0.1 to 0.4 percent.  
- Directors: 0.05 to 0.20 percent.  
- **UK:** prefer EMI options where eligible. **Greece:** use options if practical or RSUs/phantom with a clear vesting schedule.

---

## 6. Location policy and payroll mechanics

### London, UK
- Use London bands for all UK leadership regardless of remote status unless a different UK hub is defined at team level.  
- Benefits expectations: pension contribution, private medical, life assurance, and learning stipend.

### Athens, Greece
- Offers state the annual gross and the handling of Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances.  
- Benefits expectations: private medical, lunch or transport stipend, and equipment stipend for hybrid roles.  
- Do not embed exchange rates into Greek offers. State figures in EUR.

---

## 7. Offer placement rules

1) **Pick the location band first.**  
2) **Start at Q2** for solid experience at the scope defined.  
3) **Use Q3** only for scarce skills, portfolio-scale remit, or competing offers backed by evidence.  
4) **Use Q4** only with CEO and board sign-off, including a written business case.  
5) **Set the target bonus** within the range based on role impact and milestone proximity.  
6) **Add equity** aligned to level and influence.  
7) **Check internal parity** before issuing the letter.

Offer checklist is in Appendix D.

- Approve Appendix A bands and Appendix E Evidence Table.  
- Train hiring managers on location choice, quartiles, and offer scripts.  
- Update offer templates for UK and Greece with clear bonus and equity language.

### Days 31 to 60
- Run a calibration session across all live offers and open requisitions.  
- Publish a one-page quick guide per role family.  
- Switch to the new approval flow for exceptions and Q4 placements.

### Days 61 to 90
- Audit offers issued under the new policy.  
- Confirm equity pool allocation by level and set the annual refresh cadence.  
- Schedule next market refresh and governance check.

---

## 9. Risks and mitigations
- **Location resentment:** publish the location policy. Use the same titles and equity logic across locations.  
- **Compression:** review bands at every funding event and when two or more offers are above Q3.  
- **Mis-levelled roles:** require scope and outcomes to match the title. Run quarterly title hygiene checks.  
- **FX noise:** keep offers in local currency. Use an FX snapshot only for board discussion.  
- **Greek allowance confusion:** show clearly whether allowances are embedded or paid separately. Provide the calendar of instalments.

---

Your base is £XX with a target bonus of YY percent, which pays on agreed milestones. Your options are granted under the same plan as other leaders, with a four-year vest and one-year cliff.”

# Terminology fix
- **Pay quartiles**: four equal segments of the pay distribution for a role in a location.  
  - **Quartile 1 (Q1)**: lower 25 percent of base salaries  
  - **Quartile 2 (Q2)**: 25–50 percent segment  
  - **Quartile 3 (Q3)**: 50–75 percent segment  
  - **Quartile 4 (Q4)**: upper 25 percent of base salaries  
- When sources provide only a minimum and maximum, quartile boundaries are derived by evenly splitting that range as a planning proxy. When sources provide percentiles, those percentiles take precedence.  
- Any reference to time periods will say **calendar quarter** or **every three months**, never “Q1/Q2” to avoid confusion.

# Replacement copy for the white paper
Use this to replace the previous “Usage rules” and any ambiguous lines:

**How to place an offer by pay quartile**  
1) Choose the correct **location band** first.  
2) Place the offer in a **pay quartile** based on scope, calibre, scarcity, and internal parity.  
   - Start in **Quartile 2** for solid hires who meet the scope.  
   - Use **Quartile 3** for scarce skills or larger remit.  
   - Use **Quartile 4** only with a written business case and approvals.  
3) Set a **target bonus** within the stated range for the level and tie it to clear milestones.  
4) Add **equity** aligned to level and impact.  
5) Confirm **internal parity** before issuing the letter.

**Bonus timing**  
- Reviews and payouts are scheduled **every three months**. The word **quartile** is never used for timing.

# Pay Architecture Brief for AA Pre-Revenue Studio Leaders  
Couch Heroes • UK and Greece • 2025

## 1) Purpose and scope  
Set fair, defensible, and stage-appropriate compensation for C-suite roles across two locations with different labour markets and benefit norms. This brief covers CEO, CTO, CFO, COO, and CPO/Head of Production. Figures are expressed as base-salary quartiles, plus target bonus and equity guidance suitable for a AA studio before first commercial revenue. Where UK games-specific executive data exists, it is used; where not, we use current UK executive benchmarks and Athens executive benchmarks, then apply conservative planning bands for a pre-revenue games studio. SeedLegals, Index Ventures and Vestd inform equity practice. citeturn0search0turn0search2turn1search4turn1search7turn7view0turn8view0turn10search3turn11search2turn11search5

## 2) What quartiles mean and how to use them  
Quartiles split a market range into four equal bands.  
• Q1: entry to lower-mid market  
• Q2: solid market median positioning  
• Q3: upper-mid for scarce or high-impact hires  
• Q4: top-of-market for exceptional, proven leaders

For a AA pre-revenue studio, default cash positioning should be Q1–Q2 in London and Athens, with upside delivered through milestone-linked bonuses and equity. This preserves runway while remaining competitive for capability and leadership calibre.

## 3) Cross-border policy choices that matter  
1) Contracting location drives statutory benefits and practice  
• UK: auto-enrolment pension, typical private medical, and UK-friendly share schemes. EMI options are available for qualifying UK employees and are tax-advantaged. Equity pools of 5–15 percent are normal in UK startups and scaleups. citeturn10search0turn10search3  
• Greece: statutory Christmas, Easter and vacation allowances result in 14 monthly payments by law for many private-sector employees. Always quote and compare annualised base, not “per month,” to avoid misalignment. citeturn2search3turn2search4

2) Stage alignment  
Before revenue, keep cash conservative and shift value into equity and milestone bonuses defined by build, launch, and first revenue KPIs. After revenue or funding step-ups, you can re-tier individuals into higher quartiles.

3) Role clarity  
If a single leader spans multiple functions in early formation, choose the market anchor that best matches the most scarce skill and largest value driver, then adjust responsibilities and bonus measures accordingly.

## 4) UK and Greece leadership planning bands (2025)  
The tables below show total base salary planning ranges split into quartiles. Ranges come from current guides and surveys, adjusted to fit a AA, pre-revenue games studio. Bonuses and equity are expressed as policy guidance, not guaranteed amounts.

## 5) Variable pay design that fits a AA, pre-revenue studio  
1) Bonuses should be milestone-linked and capped before revenue  
• Keep CEO, CFO, COO caps lower until first revenue or funding step.  
• CTO and CPO bonuses should be tied to build cadence, quality bars, and on-time release gates, not hours or headcount.  
• In the UK, industry-wide bonuses vary widely. For startups, tie awards to concrete delivery and revenue events, not vague objectives. Avoid “discretionary only.”  

2) Equity should carry the long-term upside  
• UK option pools: 5–15 percent is the norm, with 10 percent a common target pre-Series A. Europe concentrates more equity at executive levels than the US, so plan your pool accordingly. citeturn10search0turn10search3turn11search5  
• Indicative grants for outside hires at AA stage: CEO 2–5 percent, CTO 0.5–2 percent, CFO and COO 0.25–1 percent, CPO 0.25–1 percent. Use four-year vesting with a one-year cliff and add double-trigger acceleration for a change in control. These ranges align with European startup practice and widely cited benchmarks. citeturn11search2turn11search7turn11search13

## 6) Benefits alignment by location  
• UK: auto-enrolment pension, private medical and life assurance are market standard for executives. EMI options are tax-efficient for eligible employees. Equity in the UK parent is simplest if you expect future UK funding. citeturn10search0  
• Greece: 14-month pay practice can apply. Provide private medical and life assurance to maintain parity with UK exec packages. Set equity in the same top-level entity to keep governance simple. citeturn2search3turn2search4

## 7) Using the tables to make offers  
1) Pick the quartile based on stage and proof  
• Default to Q1–Q2 for pre-revenue leaders.  
• Move to Q3–Q4 only when the candidate brings multiple shipped AA/AAA titles or rare skill combinations, or when you are post-funding and competing with AAA studios for the same individual.

2) Structure the offer  
• Base within the chosen quartile.  
• Bonus with clear guardrails and dated milestones.  
• Equity sized to create real upside and reduce cash pressure.

3) Review cadence  
Re-benchmark annually. Refresh leadership pay on funding close, at commercial launch, and at first meaningful revenue, not only on anniversaries. UK games leadership pay, especially for Studio Director and Executive Producer, tightened upwards in 2025, so revisit ranges at least yearly. citeturn0search0

## 8) Evidence and source notes  
• UK games leadership context and role mapping: TechNET Immersive Salary Survey 2025. Executive Producer, Studio Director and Head of Studio bands inform the premium between senior production and C-level product leadership in London. citeturn0search0  
• UK CTO and CPO London bands: Morgan McKinley 2025 salary guide. citeturn1search2turn1search5  
• UK CFO band breadth reference: Robert Walters 2025 UK salary guide. citeturn1search7  
• UK startup CEO planning anchor: Glassdoor Startup CEO London typical pay range (25th–75th) for 2025. Chosen to reflect pre-revenue constraints rather than FTSE norms. citeturn4search1  
• Greece executive quartiles: ERI SalaryExpert Athens and Greece 2025 pages for CTO, CFO, COO, CEO, and Athens product leadership proxy. citeturn1search1turn7view0turn8view0turn6open0turn9search9  
• Equity norms: SeedLegals option pool guidance and 2024-2025 reports; Index Ventures OptionPlan and Rewarding Talent. citeturn10search0turn10search3turn10search9turn11search2turn11search5  
• Greek 14-month pay: Eurofound and Hellenic Labour Inspectorate. citeturn2search3turn2search4

[ASSISTANT]
Here is a clean section you can drop into the white paper. It calibrates **pay quartiles by skill level and tenure in the seat**, with clear rules managers can apply in both London and Athens.

# 9) Calibrating pay by skill and tenure

## 9.1 Definitions used in this section
- **Pay quartiles**: four equal segments of the market range for a role in a location. Q1 is the lower quarter, Q4 is the upper quarter.
- **Skill level**
  - **Minimum**: meets core role requirements, limited track record at the scope; needs guidance on studio process or platform specifics.
  - **Mid**: consistently meets scope, solves problems independently, demonstrates cross-team influence, credible hiring bar setter.
  - **High**: top decile for the market, shipped multiple titles or platforms at similar or larger scale, mentors other leaders, sets discipline standards.
- **Tenure in seat**
  - **New**: 0–12 months in the role at this scope.
  - **Established**: 12–36 months in the role at this scope.
  - **Veteran**: 36+ months in the role at this scope.

Notes
- Skill is assessed against the **current scope**. If the scope grows materially, reassess both skill and band.
- Tenure alone does not justify movement between quartiles. Movement requires evidence of outcomes at the current scope.

## 9.2 Mapping matrix: skill × tenure to pay quartile, bonus, and equity refresh
This matrix applies to both London and Athens. Use the local band for the role, then choose the quartile from this mapping.

| Skill level | Tenure | Recommended pay quartile | Target bonus placement | Equity refresh guidance |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Minimum | New | Q1 | Floor of range | None in year 1. Make eligible from next grant cycle if targets met. |
| Minimum | Established | Q1 to low Q2 | Lower third of range | Consider small refresh only if performance is strong and scope widened. |
| Minimum | Veteran | Q2 | Lower to mid range | Small refresh at next pool review if business case is clear. |
| Mid | New | Q2 | Mid range | Standard grant only. No off-cycle refresh in first 12 months. |
| Mid | Established | Mid to high Q2 | Mid to upper range | Light refresh at annual cycle if delivering above plan. |
| Mid | Veteran | Low Q3 | Upper range | Refresh appropriate if leading wider initiatives or mentoring other leads. |
| High | New | Q2 to low Q3 | Mid to upper range | Front-load standard grant within policy; add milestone-based top-up, not higher cash. |
| High | Established | Q3 | Upper range | Refresh in line with impact and retention risk. |
| High | Veteran | High Q3 to Q4* | Upper range | Refresh reserved for outsized scope or retention risk, subject to board approval. |

\* Use Q4 only with a written business case that cites scarcity, proven outcomes at this scope, or a competing offer. CEO and board approval required.

## 9.3 Country overlays
- **London, UK**: apply the London band. Do not discount for hybrid arrangements that report into a London hub. Bonus and equity practice are unchanged.
- **Athens, Greece**: apply the Athens band. Quote annualised base and state clearly whether Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are included or paid as separate instalments. The quartile mapping itself does not change.

## 9.4 Progression rules and expected timing
- **Within-quartile movement**: adjust within Q1 or Q2 at the annual merit cycle when performance is strong and targets are met.  
- **Between-quartile movement**: require one or more of the following, documented in the review file:
  - Shipped or exited a major milestone at scope with quality, time, and budget outcomes.
  - Expanded remit that changes team size, budget, or platform responsibility.
  - Demonstrated repeatable hiring and leadership bar setting for the discipline.
- **Promotion to next level**: not handled by quartile changes. Run a levelling review and re-band the role.

## 9.5 Worked examples

### Executive Producer, London
Published 2025 base range: **£70,000–£95,000**. Derived pay quartiles:
- Q1 £70,000–£76,000
- Q2 £76,000–£83,000
- Q3 £83,000–£89,000
- Q4 £89,000–£95,000

Placement examples
- **Minimum skill, New**: Q1 placement, for example £74,000 with a 15 percent target bonus. Equity at the standard Director-level grant.  
- **Mid skill, Established**: mid Q2, for example £81,000 with a 20 percent target bonus. Eligible for a light equity refresh at the next cycle.  
- **High skill, Established**: Q3, for example £88,000 with a 25 percent target bonus. Consider a refresh if the remit includes multiple teams or live ops.

### CTO, Athens
Published 2025 base range: **€67,000–€124,000**. Derived pay quartiles:
- Q1 €67,000–€81,000
- Q2 €81,000–€95,000
- Q3 €95,000–€110,000
- Q4 €110,000–€124,000

Placement examples
- **Mid skill, New**: Q2, for example €90,000 with a 20 percent target bonus. Contract clarifies the treatment of Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances.  
- **High skill, Established**: Q3, for example €108,000 with a 25 percent target bonus. Equity at 0.8 percent if impact and scarcity justify.  
- **High skill, Veteran**: high Q3. Q4 only with board approval and a documented retention or scarcity case.

## 9.6 Manager checklist for consistent decisions
1) Confirm location band.  
2) Assess skill level against the current scope.  
3) Confirm tenure bracket.  
4) Select the pay quartile from the matrix and set bonus within the stated range.  
5) Apply equity only through the standard grant or the annual refresh cycle.  
6) Run an internal parity check before issuing the offer or adjustment.

# 9) Calibrating pay by capability tier and time in role

## 9.1 Definitions
- **Pay quartiles**: four equal segments of the market range for a role in a location. Q1 is the lower quarter, Q4 is the upper quarter.
- **Capability tier**
  - **Foundational**: meets core requirements for the role at this scope, building breadth and studio-specific fluency.
  - **Proficient**: consistently delivers at scope, solves complex problems independently, influences across teams, sets hiring standards.
  - **Expert**: top decile in the market, multiple shipped titles or platforms at similar or larger scale, mentors other leaders, sets discipline strategy.
- **Time in role**
  - **Newly appointed**: 0 to 12 months at this scope.
  - **Established**: 12 to 36 months at this scope.
  - **Seasoned**: more than 36 months at this scope.

Notes  
- Assess capability against the **current scope**. If scope grows materially, reassess both capability and band.  
- Time in role does not, on its own, justify movement between quartiles. Movement requires evidence of outcomes at the current scope.

## 9.2 Mapping matrix: capability × time in role to pay quartile, bonus, and equity refresh

| Capability tier | Time in role | Recommended pay quartile | Target bonus placement | Equity refresh guidance |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Foundational | Newly appointed | Q1 | Floor of range | None in year 1. Eligible from next grant cycle if targets met. |
| Foundational | Established | Q1 to low Q2 | Lower third of range | Small refresh only if performance is strong and scope widened. |
| Foundational | Seasoned | Q2 | Lower to mid range | Consider light refresh at next pool review if business case is clear. |
| Proficient | Newly appointed | Q2 | Mid range | Standard grant only. No off-cycle refresh in first 12 months. |
| Proficient | Established | Mid to high Q2 | Mid to upper range | Light refresh at annual cycle if delivering above plan. |
| Proficient | Seasoned | Low Q3 | Upper range | Refresh appropriate if leading wider initiatives or mentoring other leads. |
| Expert | Newly appointed | Q2 to low Q3 | Mid to upper range | Front-load standard grant within policy; add milestone top-up rather than higher cash. |
| Expert | Established | Q3 | Upper range | Refresh in line with impact and retention risk. |
| Expert | Seasoned | High Q3 to Q4* | Upper range | Refresh reserved for outsized scope or retention risk, subject to board approval. |

\* Use Q4 only with a written business case that cites scarcity, proven outcomes at this scope, or a competing offer. CEO and board approval required.

- **Between-quartile movement**: require documented evidence such as shipped milestones at scope, expanded remit, or sustained leadership impact.  
- **Promotion to next level**: not handled by quartile changes. Run a levelling review and re-band the role.

### CTO, Athens  
Published 2025 base range: **€67,000–€124,000**. Derived pay quartiles:  
Q1 €67,000–€81,000; Q2 €81,000–€95,000; Q3 €95,000–€110,000; Q4 €110,000–€124,000.

- **Expert, Established**: Q3, for example €108,000 with a 25 percent target bonus. Equity at 0.8 percent if impact and scarcity justify.  
- **Expert, Seasoned**: high Q3. Q4 only with board approval and a documented retention or scarcity case.

[ASSISTANT]
Good catch, and thanks for the context. Since both CEO and COO are founders, and you want equitable pay across all C-level, here’s a clean founder-appropriate framework that keeps cash fair, separates investor returns from salary, and prevents role inversions.

# Founder C-level pay framework

## 1) Principles
- **Equitable cash at the same level:** founders and non-founders at C-level are placed in the same **pay quartile** for their role and location unless there is a documented scope or performance reason.
- **Separate investor returns from salary:** the CEO’s seed capital is recognised through an instrument (convertible note, founder loan, or paid-in equity), not via higher salary.
- **No inversion:** the CEO’s base is set at or above the highest functional executive’s median in the same location. Exceptions require a written case and board approval.
- **Location anchored:** use London bands for UK contracts and Athens bands for Greek contracts. Quote annualised base in local currency. For Greece, always state how Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are handled.

## 2) How to set cash right now (pre-revenue)
Choose one of these two normalisation paths and apply it to **all** C-level so pay is equitable.

**Path A — Immediate parity:** place every C-level at **Quartile 2** of their location band.  
Use Q3 only for scarcity or outsized scope with evidence.

**Path B — Staged parity:** place every C-level at **high Quartile 1** now, with a written step-up to **Quartile 2** on the earliest of: funding close, vertical slice exit, or soft-launch KPI gate. This helps runway while keeping equity across the team.

## 3) Founder CEO with personal capital
Pick one, document it, and keep salary separate:

- **Convertible note:** market discount and interest, converts at next equity round. Cleanest for investors, keeps salary neutral.
- **Founder loan:** fixed interest and repayment schedule. Use only if near-term cash flow allows repayment.
- **Paid-in capital (equity):** treat as additional founder equity. Salary remains based on the role band, not the investment.

Governance: the board (or a two-director comp committee) approves the instrument and records it separately from payroll.

## 4) What “equitable” looks like in numbers
Below are **planning placements** for founders at **Quartile 2** in each location, using the 2025 bands we built for a AA, pre-revenue studio. If your CEO or COO sit in different cities, apply the correct location band to each person.

### London, UK — Quartile 2 placements (examples)
- **CEO (founder):** Q2 placement within £196k–£218k base. Target bonus 25–40 percent with milestone gates.  
- **COO (founder):** Q2 placement within £130k–£140k base. Target bonus 15–30 percent tied to build cadence and release readiness.  
- **Other C-level (non-founder or founder):** place in Q2 of their role band for London to maintain equity at the level.

### Athens, Greece — Quartile 2 placements (examples)
- **CEO (founder):** Q2 placement within €210k–€240k base. Target bonus 20–35 percent.  
- **COO (founder):** Q2 placement within €144k–€185k base. Target bonus 10–25 percent.  
Notes for Greece: quote the **annualised** figure and state whether Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are included or paid separately.

These placements keep the CEO’s base above other functions in the same location, satisfy the non-inversion guardrail, and give you a consistent message to the board and candidates.

## 5) Equity to balance runway and fairness
- Keep equity **location-agnostic**.  
- Indicative founder grants at AA stage remain: CEO 2–5 percent; COO 0.25–1 percent; other C-level 0.25–1 percent. Four-year vest, one-year cliff.  
- If you use Path B (staged parity), do **not** over-use equity to compensate for a temporary cash discount; use the scheduled step-up to Q2 instead.

## 6) Offer language you can reuse
“Your role is based in [London/Athens]. We set leadership pay by location and **pay quartile**. As a member of the C-team, we place leaders at **Quartile 2** before revenue to keep the structure equitable across functions. Your base is [local currency amount] with a [X percent] target bonus tied to agreed studio milestones. Your founder investment is recognised separately via a [convertible note/founder loan/paid-in capital], which does not affect salary.”

Here is a blunt, senior-level critique with concrete fixes. I am writing as a veteran CEO and COO, and as an executive comp consultant evaluating whether this delivery gives two founders a safe, decision-grade guide.

# Executive verdict
Directionally useful, but not yet decision-grade for founders who are careful with spend and new to comp design. It needs clearer “how to use” flow, stronger evidence signalling on every number, explicit runway modes that change cash, bonus and equity, and harder guardrails to stop accidental inversions or over-spend. With the fixes below, it becomes a 10 of 10.

# What the current delivery gets right
- Uses pay quartiles instead of single numbers, which reduces anchoring risk.
- Separates London and Athens, and shows alternate currency in brackets for fast comparison.
- Calls out Greek allowance practice and annualises pay to keep apples to apples.
- Provides capability and time-in-role mapping so you can place people consistently.
- Puts CEO above functional leads to avoid obvious inversions.

# Where it misses your brief and how to fix it
1) **Confidence on the numbers is unclear.**  
   Add an Evidence Table with a confidence column for each role and city, plus a refresh date. Mark any role where we inferred a band from adjacent roles as “inferred” rather than “observed.”

2) **Not enough stage control for careful founders.**  
   Introduce three studio “runway modes” that explicitly change cash, bonus caps and equity. See the Runway Modes table below.

3) **Decision flow is split across sections.**  
   Add a one-page “How to decide pay in 5 steps” that leaders can actually follow on a call. I drafted it below.

4) **Bonus design is too generic.**  
   Replace ranges with per-role scorecards and caps by mode, and state the payout formula. Include a clawback for misstatement or gross under-performance.

5) **Equity policy lacks guardrails.**  
   Add pool size, grant bands by role, vesting rules, and two special rules: no cash for equity trade-ups, and board approval for any grant above the band.

6) **Founder investment is not fully ring-fenced.**  
   State that salary is independent of founder cash invested, and recognise investment only through a note or paid-in equity recorded outside payroll.

7) **Athens 14-month practice could still confuse.**  
   Force a standard contract sentence that states whether Christmas, Easter and leave allowances are included in the quoted annual base or paid separately, and show the monthly split.

8) **Parity and inversion controls are implicit, not binding.**  
   Add a written non-inversion rule and a peer-parity check before any Q3 or Q4 placement.

9) **No operating budget link.**  
   Tie total leadership cash to a percentage envelope of non-vendor Opex by mode. This is how you stay careful with spend.

10) **FX snapshot governance.**  
    Keep the alternate currency in brackets, but fix a snapshot date and state that offers are always made in the local currency.

# Concrete upgrades to insert now

## A) One-page “How to decide pay in 5 steps” (paste into the guide)
1) Pick the **location band** for the legal employing entity.  
2) Select a **runway mode** below that matches the next 6 months.  
3) Choose a **pay quartile** using the capability and time-in-role matrix.  
4) Set **bonus** from the role scorecard for your mode.  
5) Set **equity** from the grant band. Run parity and inversion checks. Issue the letter in local currency. Log the Evidence Table row.

## B) Runway modes that change cash, bonus and equity
| Mode | When to use | Base positioning | Bonus cap | Equity stance |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Lean runway | < 9 months runway or pre-funding, high uncertainty | Q1 to low Q2 | CEO 25%, other C-level 20% | Grants at lower half of band; no off-cycle refresh |
| Base | 9 to 18 months runway or funding signed, build predictable | Q2 | CEO 35%, other C-level 25% | Grants mid-band; refresh only at annual cycle |
| Growth | > 18 months runway or live revenue, hiring for scale | High Q2 to Q3 | CEO 40%, other C-level 30% | Grants at upper half for scarcest roles; refresh allowed with written case |

## C) Role scorecards and bonus math
Use this payout formula for all roles: Payout = Target Bonus × Weighted KPI Score, capped by mode.

**CEO example**  
- Funding or revenue gate 40 percent  
- Delivery gates passed 30 percent  
- Team health and senior hiring 20 percent  
- Board reporting hygiene 10 percent  
Cap by mode as in the table above.

**COO example**  
- Release readiness gates passed 40 percent  
- Throughput vs plan 30 percent  
- Quality bars met 20 percent  
- Org hygiene and cost discipline 10 percent

Similar 4-line scorecards should be added for CFO, CTO, CPO and Executive Producer with the right KPIs.

## D) Equity grant bands and rules
- CEO 2 to 5 percent. CTO, CFO, COO, CPO 0.25 to 1 percent. EP 0.1 to 0.3 percent. Four year vest, one year cliff.  
- No cash-for-equity swaps.  
- Any grant above the band needs a written case and board approval.  
- Double trigger acceleration on change of control only.

## E) Non-inversion and parity checks
- **Non-inversion**: hired CEO base at or above the highest functional leader’s median in the same city.  
- **Parity**: before issuing an offer at Q3 or Q4, compare against peers at level in the same city and record the rationale.

## F) Budget envelope control
- Total C-team base and target bonuses should fit inside a budget envelope that is a fixed percentage of non-vendor Opex for the next two quarters:  
  - Lean runway 20 to 25 percent  
  - Base 25 to 30 percent  
  - Growth 30 to 35 percent  
This gives you a hard stop if offers start creeping up.

## G) Contract language for Athens
Include this sentence in offers:  
“The annual base figure above is quoted on an annualised basis. Christmas, Easter and leave allowances are [included in the figure and paid monthly] or [paid as separate instalments], per Greek practice.”

## H) Evidence Table pattern to add at the end of the guide

|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|

Here is the add-on you asked for. It gives you a clean, founder-safe way to treat UK and Greece staff fairly on cash and equity, while keeping the CEO’s control intact. You can paste this into the white paper as a new section titled “Location Parity and Founder Control.”

# Location parity and founder control

## 1) What “fair” means across London and Athens
- Cash is location anchored. Use the London or Athens quartile bands for base pay and bonus targets.
- Equity is location agnostic. The same role and level gets the same grant range, regardless of the city.
- Benefits align locally. In Greece, always state whether Christmas, Easter and leave allowances are included in the annualised base or paid as separate instalments.
- Mobility neutrality. If a leader relocates between London and Athens, equity is unchanged and cash moves to the new location band at the nearest review.

## 2) Equity grant bands to use in both locations
- CEO: 2 to 5 percent
- CTO, CFO, COO, CPO: 0.25 to 1.0 percent
- Executive Producer: 0.10 to 0.30 percent
- Vesting: 4 years, 1-year cliff, monthly thereafter
- Change in control: double-trigger acceleration only
- No cash for equity trade-ups. Any grant above band needs a written case and board approval

## 3) Option pool design and refresh rules
- Start pool at 10 to 15 percent unallocated.
- Refresh only at financing events or when signed hiring plans require it.
- Refresh sizing is negotiated to be pre-money so all existing shareholders dilute pro rata, not only founders.
- Do not promise off-cycle refreshes. Use the annual cycle unless a financing event sets a new baseline.

## 4) Guardrails that preserve CEO control
Pick your control line now and stick to it in every negotiation.

- Control line through Seed: CEO ≥ 50.1 percent post-transaction
- Control line through Series A: CEO ≥ 33.4 percent post-transaction plus board control rules
- Board control until Series A: 2 of 3 seats held by founders, with investor observer rights and standard protective provisions
- Founder participation rights: founders have a pro-rata right in each round to maintain their percentage
- Pool increases come from the pre-money, not solely from founder shares

## 5) Worked cap table scenarios that keep control and fairness

### Scenario A: Typical and safe
Pre-transaction  
- CEO 70 percent  
- COO 15 percent  
- Advisor 3 percent  
- ESOP 12 percent

Seed round sells 20 percent new shares, and ESOP refreshes to 15 percent post-money. Post-transaction ownership  
- Investors 20 percent  
- ESOP 15 percent  
- Founders and advisor 65 percent total  
- CEO becomes 70 ÷ 88 × 65 = **51.6 percent**  
- COO becomes 15 ÷ 88 × 65 = **11.1 percent**

Result: CEO stays above 50 percent. Equity is location agnostic, so London and Athens hires draw from the same ESOP without upsetting control.

### Scenario B: Tight but acceptable
Pre-transaction  
- CEO 60 percent  
- COO 15 percent  
- Advisor 3 percent  
- ESOP 12 percent

Same financing terms as Scenario A. Post-transaction ownership  
- Investors 20 percent  
- ESOP 15 percent  
- Founders and advisor 65 percent total  
- CEO becomes 60 ÷ 78 × 65 = **50.0 percent**

Result: CEO sits on the control line. Any additional pool top-up or a second round without participation would drop control below 50 percent, so either reduce investor take, shrink the ESOP refresh, or have the CEO exercise participation rights.

## 6) How to issue equity fairly across locations
- Grant sizing is identical for the same role and level in London and Athens.
- Quote grants as a percentage of fully diluted capital. Avoid absolute share counts in letters unless you include the fully diluted number in the same sentence.
- Use a single global equity plan for both locations if possible, with country-specific sub-plans for tax compliance. Keep vesting rules identical.

## 7) Runway-aware knobs you can turn without losing control
- Cash knob by mode  
  - Lean runway: Q1 to low Q2 base, lower bonus caps  
  - Base mode: Q2 base, standard bonus caps  
  - Growth mode: high Q2 to Q3 base, higher caps for scarce roles  
- Equity knob by scarcity  
  - Keep within bands. For truly scarce hires, move up inside the band rather than increasing the band
- Pool knob at financing  
  - Size the ESOP refresh to the signed hiring plan and negotiate it to be pre-money

## 8) Contract language to prevent UK vs Greece misunderstandings
- Include this sentence for Athens:  
  “The annual base is quoted on an annualised basis. Christmas, Easter and leave allowances are [included and paid monthly] or [paid as separate instalments] according to Greek practice.”
- Include this sentence for all equity offers:  
  “Equity is granted under the company plan and vests over four years with a one-year cliff. Percentages are stated on a fully diluted basis at grant signature.”

## 9) Quick checklist founders can run before signing any offer
1) Is the role’s cash in the correct location band and quartile  
2) Is the bonus target set from the role scorecard and the current runway mode  
3) Is the equity grant inside the band and stated as a percentage of fully diluted capital  
4) Does the ESOP still cover the signed hiring plan after this grant  
5) Do the post-offer percentages keep the CEO above the current control line  
6) For Athens, does the letter state how allowances are treated  
7) Have you recorded the Evidence Table row with source and date

If you want, I can insert this section into the Word guide you already have and include a small cap table calculator page that lets you plug in pool size, investor take, and pre-round ownership to see the CEO percentage after each round.

# Couch Heroes  
## Executive Compensation Study and Guide  
**UK and Greece, AA Studio, pre-revenue**

## Executive summary
This guide gives founders a clear, defensible way to set base pay, bonus, and equity for C-level roles in London and Athens. It converts current 2025 market signals into four pay quartiles per role and city, then adds decision rules so two careful, spend-disciplined founders can place themselves and other leaders fairly, without risking pay inversions or loss of founder control. London figures draw on 2025 recruiter benchmarks for CTO, CPO, COO and CFO, plus an Executive Producer anchor for games. Athens figures use ERI and SalaryExpert executive ranges and state the Greek 14-month pay practice so contracts are apples to apples. citeturn0search2turn0search1turn0search3turn0search4turn0search0turn1search0turn1search1turn1search2turn1search3

---

## How to decide pay in five steps
1) Pick the **location band** for the legal employing entity: London or Athens.  
2) Select the **runway mode** for the next 6 months (Lean, Base, or Growth) to scale cash, bonus caps, and equity.  
3) Choose the **pay quartile** using the capability and time-in-role matrix.  
4) Set the **bonus** from the role scorecard and your current runway mode.  
5) Set the **equity** from the grant band. Run the parity and founder-control checks before issuing the letter.

---

## Runway modes that change cash, bonus and equity
| Mode | When to use | Base positioning | Bonus cap | Equity stance |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Lean runway | Less than 9 months runway or pre-funding | Q1 to low Q2 | CEO 25%, other C-level 20% | Grants at lower half of band, no off-cycle refresh |
| Base | 9–18 months runway or signed funding | Q2 | CEO 35%, other C-level 25% | Grants mid-band, refresh only at annual cycle |
| Growth | More than 18 months runway or live revenue | High Q2 to Q3 | CEO 40%, other C-level 30% | Grants at upper half for scarcest roles, refresh on written case |

---

## Location parity and founder control
- **Cash is location-anchored.** Use London or Athens quartiles for base and bonus.  
- **Equity is location-agnostic.** Same grant bands for the same role in either city.  
- **Greek practice.** Quote Athens offers as **annualised** figures and state whether Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are included or paid separately. Greece commonly pays 14 months per year in the private sector. citeturn1search3turn1search8turn1search13  
- **Control guardrails.** Pick your founder control line and hold it: CEO at least 50.1% post-Seed or at least 33.4% plus board control post-Series A. Option pool increases are negotiated pre-money so all holders dilute pro-rata.

---

## Role scorecards and bonus maths
All roles use the same payout formula:  
**Bonus payout = Target bonus × Weighted KPI score, capped by the current runway mode.**

**CEO**: Funding or revenue gates 40%, delivery gates 30%, senior hiring and team health 20%, board hygiene 10%.  
**COO**: Release readiness 40%, throughput vs plan 30%, quality bars 20%, cost discipline 10%.  
**CFO**: Runway and reporting 40%, audit readiness 30%, fundraising support 20%, FP&A hygiene 10%.  
**CTO**: Platform stability 35%, deployment cadence 25%, security and compliance 20%, team scaling 20%.  
**CPO / Head of Production**: Roadmap delivery 35%, submission readiness 25%, live-ops preparedness 20%, quality gates 20%.  
**Executive Producer**: Scope delivery 40%, resourcing efficiency 25%, milestone outcomes 25%, cross-team comms 10%.

---

## Equity grant bands and rules
- CEO 2–5%. CTO, CFO, COO, CPO 0.25–1.0%. Executive Producer 0.10–0.30%. Four-year vest, one-year cliff.  
- No cash-for-equity swaps. Any grant above band needs a written case and board approval.  
- Double-trigger acceleration only on change of control.  
- **Pool policy.** Start with a 10–15% ESOP unallocated. Refresh only at financing or when signed plans require it. Pool refresh is negotiated pre-money.

2) Calibrate inside the quartile by capability and time in role.  
3) Set target bonus from the scorecard and runway mode.  
4) Add the equity grant from the band.

| Bonus and equity structure that founders can operate | Good bones. Role scorecards and equity bands are sensible. | 8/10 | Add a single payout formula example filled with numbers for each role and show a sample calculation. Add a “board approval” checklist for any out-of-band grant. |
| Adjusts to financial position without gaming | Strong. Runway modes and a budget envelope discipline spending. | 9/10 | Add an “auto step-up” clause template so Lean to Base mode movements are pre-agreed and do not require re-negotiation. |
| Fair treatment UK vs Greece | Good on principles and Greek allowances. | 8/10 | Show Total Cost to Company normalisation for Athens when 14-month practice is separate. Provide a monthly split example in the appendix. |
| Preserves founder control while compensating staff | Solid. Control lines, pre-money pool refresh, and participation rights are stated. | 9/10 | Add two more cap-table worked examples that include an ESOP top-up and a follow-on round to illustrate compounding dilution. |
| Helps founders set their own pay and others | Good start. Non-inversion rule, role bands and scripts help. | 8/10 | Add a one-page “Founder self-placement” aid that maps CEO and COO scope to quartiles, with the same parity checks you require for others. |

# Gaps that must be closed
1) Evidence strength and traceability  
The guide cites 2025 sources, but quartiles are produced by a linear split of the min to max range. Real market distributions are not linear. For decision-grade confidence, pin medians to observed sources and build quartiles around those medians. Use either multiple observed points per role or cross-role triangulation. Every table row should show: source name, date, observed or inferred, confidence, next refresh.

2) Athens comparability and “14-month” clarity  
You annualise and include a standard sentence, which is good. Add a Total Cost to Company example that shows an Athens offer in both 12-month and 14-month presentation so founders and candidates cannot talk past each other.

3) Tooling for founders who are not comp specialists  
The text is clear, but it still asks the reader to do mental arithmetic. Add three addenda: a one-page QuickStart, a single-page calculator grid they can fill by hand, and two fully worked offers that pass parity and control checks.

4) Equity governance under pressure  
Equity bands are sound, but founders need a hard rule when they feel forced to go out of band. Require a written business case with four bullets: scarcity proof, value proof, control impact, and ESOP sufficiency after grant. No out-of-band grant without those four.

5) FX snapshot governance  
You set a snapshot and show alternates in brackets. Add a rule that offers are always quoted and signed in local currency with a single FX footnote for board comparisons only. Note a refresh trigger if FX moves more than five percent.

# Concrete improvements to include

- Step 4: Set bonus target from the role scorecard, apply the cap for the current mode.  
- Step 5: Add equity from the band.  
- Run parity, non-inversion, budget envelope, and control checks.  
Include one fully worked London CEO example and one Athens COO example with numbers.

4) Total Cost to Company for Athens

5) Founder control calculator snippets

6) Governance inserts
