# Couch Heroes  
## Executive Compensation Study and Guide  
UK and Greece, AA studio, pre-revenue

Prepared by a senior HR and compensation consultant with CEO and COO review

### Change log for this iteration
- Added a QuickStart page with two fully worked examples that a non-specialist can follow on a call.  
- Anchored quartiles to observed 2025 medians where available, with “Observed” or “Inferred” labels and a refresh plan.  
- Added a numeric bonus example that shows the payout calculation.  
- Added Athens “Total Cost to Company” normalisation and a monthly split example for 14-month practice.  
- Hardened equity governance with an out-of-band grant checklist and an auto step-up clause tied to runway mode changes.  
- Expanded cap-table scenarios, including ESOP top-ups and a follow-on round, and added a simple control test founders can run.  
- Kept equity location-agnostic to ensure fairness between UK and Greece.  
- Kept alternate currency in parentheses for quick comparisons and stated the FX snapshot rule.  

---

## 1) QuickStart: how to decide pay in five steps
1. Pick the **location band** for the employing entity: London or Athens.  
2. Select the **runway mode** for the next six months: Lean, Base, or Growth.  
3. Choose a **pay quartile** using the capability and time-in-role matrix.  
4. Set the **bonus** from the role scorecard and apply the mode cap.  
5. Set the **equity** from the grant band, then run the Parity, Non-inversion, Budget, and Control checks.

### Worked example A: CEO in London, Base mode
- Location band: London CEO band £200,000 to £260,000 (EUR shown in parentheses in the detailed table).  
- Capability and time in role: Expert, Established. Choose Quartile 2.  
- Base placement: £210,000 (with EUR equivalent in parentheses).  
- Bonus: target 35 percent. Scorecard weights applied below.  
- Equity: 3.0 percent, four-year vest, one-year cliff.  
- Checks: CEO base is above top functional median in London. Total C-team cash inside the Base mode budget envelope. Post-grant ESOP still covers the hiring plan. CEO remains above the control line selected by the board.

### Worked example B: COO in Athens, Lean mode with auto step-up
- Location band: Athens COO band.  
- Capability and time in role: Proficient, Newly appointed. Choose Quartile 1 with a pre-agreed step to Quartile 2 at the first soft-launch gate.  
- Base placement: Quartile 1 figure per the Athens table.  
- Bonus: cap 20 percent in Lean mode with readiness and throughput KPIs.  
- Equity: 0.40 percent within the COO band.  
- Contract sentence: state clearly whether Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are included in the annualised base or paid as separate instalments.  
- FX note: offer letter is in EUR only. GBP is shown in parentheses for comparability in internal discussions.

---

## 2) Runway modes that change cash, bonus, and equity
| Mode | When to use | Base positioning | Bonus cap | Equity stance |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Lean runway | Less than 9 months runway or pre-funding | Quartile 1 to low Quartile 2 | CEO 25 percent. Other C-level 20 percent | Grants at lower half of band. No off-cycle refresh |
| Base | 9 to 18 months runway or funding signed | Quartile 2 | CEO 35 percent. Other C-level 25 percent | Grants mid-band. Refresh only at annual cycle |
| Growth | More than 18 months runway or live revenue | High Quartile 2 to Quartile 3 | CEO 40 percent. Other C-level 30 percent | Grants at upper half for scarcest roles with a written case |

**Budget envelope control**  
Fit total C-team base and target bonus inside a percentage of non-vendor Opex for the next two quarters: Lean 20 to 25 percent, Base 25 to 30 percent, Growth 30 to 35 percent.

**Auto step-up clause**  
“Base pay moves from Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 on the earliest of: soft-launch gate passed, funding close, or revenue run-rate threshold. Bonus cap moves from Lean to Base at the same time.”

---

## 3) Location parity and founder control
- **Cash is location-anchored**. Use London or Athens quartiles for base and bonus.  
- **Equity is location-agnostic**. Same grant bands for the same level in both cities.  
- **Greek practice**. Quote Athens offers as annualised figures. State whether Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are included or paid separately.  
- **Founder control guardrails**. Select a control line now and hold it. Seed: CEO at least 50.1 percent post-transaction. Through Series A: CEO at least 33.4 percent with board control safeguards. ESOP refreshes are negotiated pre-money so all holders dilute pro rata.

---

## 4) Capability and time-in-role matrix
| Capability | 0 to 12 months | 12 to 36 months | 36 months plus |
|---|---|---|---|
| Foundational | Quartile 1 to low Quartile 2 | Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 | Quartile 2 |
| Proficient | Quartile 2 | Mid to high Quartile 2 | Low Quartile 3 |
| Expert | Quartile 2 to low Quartile 3 | Quartile 3 | High Quartile 3 to Quartile 4 |

---

## 5) Bonus design and a numeric example
**Payout formula**  
Bonus payout = Target bonus × Weighted KPI score, subject to the mode cap.

**CEO scorecard example**  
- Funding or revenue gate 40 percent  
- Delivery gates passed 30 percent  
- Senior hiring and team health 20 percent  
- Board reporting hygiene 10 percent

**Example calculation**  
Target bonus 35 percent. KPI scores: 0.9, 0.8, 0.7, 1.0.  
Weighted KPI score = (0.9 × 0.40) + (0.8 × 0.30) + (0.7 × 0.20) + (1.0 × 0.10) = 0.86.  
Payout = 0.35 × 0.86 = 0.301. That equals 30.1 percent of base, within the Base mode cap.

Role scorecards for COO, CFO, CTO, CPO, and Executive Producer follow the same four-line pattern with role-appropriate KPIs.

---

## 6) Equity grant bands and approval rules
- CEO 2.0 to 5.0 percent.  
- CTO, CFO, COO, CPO 0.25 to 1.0 percent.  
- Executive Producer 0.10 to 0.30 percent.  
- Vesting 4 years with a 1-year cliff.  
- Change of control uses double-trigger acceleration only.  
- **Out-of-band grant checklist**. No grant above band without a written case that covers scarcity proof, value proof, control impact, and ESOP sufficiency.

**Option pool policy**  
Start at 10 to 15 percent unallocated. Refresh at financing or when signed hiring plans require it. Refresh is negotiated pre-money.

---

## 7) Athens Total Cost to Company and monthly split
Two ways to present the same annualised base. Quote both in the appendix of the offer to avoid confusion.

**Example**  
Annualised base: €180,000.

- If paid as 14-month practice: monthly base €180,000 ÷ 14 = €12,857. Christmas pays one extra month, Easter pays half a month, leave pays half a month.  
- If equalised to 12 months: monthly base €180,000 ÷ 12 = €15,000.  
- Total over the year is the same. State clearly which method applies in the contract.

**Standard sentence for Athens**  
“The annual base above is quoted on an annualised basis. Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are [included and paid monthly] or [paid as separate instalments] according to Greek practice.”

---

## 8) FX snapshot and display rule
Tables show the local currency first with the alternate currency in parentheses. Fix an FX snapshot date for internal comparisons. Offers are always issued and paid in the local currency of contract. Refresh the snapshot if rates move by more than five percent.

---

## 9) Quartile tables and evidence discipline
- Quartiles are anchored to observed 2025 medians where available.  
- Rows are labelled **Observed** or **Inferred**.  
- The Evidence Table at the back notes source, date, confidence, and next refresh.  
- Equity remains location-agnostic to avoid UK versus Greece inequity.  
- The CEO band in each city is a policy anchor set above the highest functional median to prevent role inversion.

(Use the latest tables you accepted in the prior draft. They already display London values in GBP with EUR in parentheses and Athens values in EUR with GBP in parentheses. Keep those numbers and labels, and update only as new 2025 data is observed.)

---

## 10) Founder control scenarios and quick test
**Control quick test**  
If a financing sets Investors = p percent post and ESOP post-refresh = e percent, all pre-round holders share the remaining 1 − p − e. A founder’s post percentage is Founder pre percentage × (1 − p − e). Use this to sanity check control quickly.

### Scenario A: Safe Seed with ESOP refresh
- Pre: CEO 60 percent.  
- Target post: Investors 20 percent, ESOP 15 percent.  
- CEO post = 60 percent × (1 − 0.20 − 0.15) = 60 percent × 0.65 = **39.0 percent**.  
Result: below the 50.1 percent Seed control line. Options: reduce investor take, reduce pool, or have CEO buy into the round to increase ownership.

### Scenario B: Strong pre with higher founder stake
- Pre: CEO 75 percent.  
- Same post targets: Investors 20 percent, ESOP 15 percent.  
- CEO post = 75 percent × 0.65 = **48.8 percent**.  
Still below 50.1 percent. Either shrink investor take to 18 percent, set ESOP to 12 percent, or combine both.

### Scenario C: Balanced plan to keep control
- Choose Investors 18 percent and ESOP 12 percent post.  
- CEO post = 75 percent × (1 − 0.18 − 0.12) = 75 percent × 0.70 = **52.5 percent**.  
Result: above the control line with a credible pool.

### Scenario D: Follow-on round after Scenario C
- Series A sells 20 percent new shares and refreshes ESOP to 15 percent post.  
- The pre-Series A holders share becomes 65 percent.  
- CEO new post = 52.5 percent × 0.65 = **34.1 percent**.  
Result: acceptable only if the Series A governance keeps effective control through board structure. Otherwise plan a participation right for the CEO to buy a portion of the round.

---

## 11) Offer scripts you can reuse today
**CEO, London, Base mode**  
“We set leadership pay by city and pay quartile. For CEO London the base band is £200,000 to £260,000. Based on scope and track record we are placing in Quartile 2 at £210,000 with a 35 percent target bonus tied to funding, delivery gates, and team health. Options vest over four years with a one-year cliff.”

**COO, Athens, Lean mode with auto step-up**  
“This role uses the Athens band. Given Lean runway we place base in Quartile 1 with an automatic step to Quartile 2 at the first soft-launch gate. Bonus is capped at 20 percent and tied to readiness and throughput. The contract states whether Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are included or paid as separate instalments.”

---

## 12) Governance checklist
- Correct city band and quartile chosen.  
- Bonus target set from scorecard and mode cap applied.  
- Equity within band. No out-of-band grant without the four-point written case.  
- Budget envelope respected for the current mode.  
- Non-inversion and peer parity checked and recorded.  
- Control quick test passed at the current round plan.  
- Athens letters include the allowances sentence when relevant.  
- Evidence Table updated with source, date, confidence, and next refresh.

# Couch Heroes  
## Executive Compensation Study and Guide  
UK and Greece, AA studio, pre-revenue

Prepared by an executive compensation advisor with CEO and COO review

### Purpose
Give two founders a practical and defensible way to set their own pay and to compensate other C-level leaders in London and Athens. The guide translates current 2025 market signals into four pay quartiles per role and city, adds simple decisions that reflect financial position, and protects founder control while treating UK and Greece staff fairly.

### How to use this guide
1. Identify the employing entity and select the London or Athens band.  
2. Choose your runway mode for the next six months.  
3. Place the role in a pay quartile using the capability and time-in-role matrix.  
4. Select the bonus target from the role scorecard and apply the mode cap.  
5. Grant equity from the band. Run the parity, non-inversion, budget, FX and founder-control checks.

---

## 1. Principles we will hold to
- Pay is set by location for cash and bonus. Equity is location agnostic for the same level.  
- Quartiles provide structured room to place individuals without breaking internal parity.  
- Bonuses pay on delivery, not narrative. Scorecards are short, weighted, and auditable.  
- Equity banding keeps offers competitive without inviting dilution drift.  
- Founder investment is recognised through instruments, not salary.  
- Offers are always made and paid in the local currency of contract. Alternate currency is shown in parentheses for comparison only.

---

## 2. Method in brief
- Ranges are anchored to current 2025 sources and normalised to local currency.  
- Quartiles are presented as Q1 to Q4 from the observed market range. Where a market median is available, placement guidance references it. Where a role lacks direct data in Athens, the row is labelled inferred and will be refreshed first.  
- Tables display local currency first and alternate currency in parentheses. Conversions follow a fixed FX snapshot so internal comparisons are consistent.

---

## 3. Location fairness and Greek practice
- London pay reflects UK cost of labour and market competition for senior talent.  
- Athens pay often uses a 14-month practice in the private sector. Quote Athens offers as annualised figures and state whether Christmas, Easter and leave allowances are included in the annualised number or paid as separate instalments.  
- If a leader relocates between cities, equity is unchanged and cash moves to the new location band at the next review.

---

## 4. Runway modes that adjust cash, bonus and equity
| Mode | When to use | Base placement | Bonus cap | Equity stance |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Lean runway | Less than nine months of runway or pre-funding | Quartile 1 to low Quartile 2 | CEO 25 percent, other C-level 20 percent | Grants at the lower half of band, no off-cycle refresh |
| Base | Nine to eighteen months of runway or funding signed | Quartile 2 | CEO 35 percent, other C-level 25 percent | Grants mid-band, refresh at annual cycle only |
| Growth | More than eighteen months of runway or live revenue | High Quartile 2 to Quartile 3 | CEO 40 percent, other C-level 30 percent | Grants at upper half for scarce roles with a written case |

Budget discipline  
Keep combined C-team base plus target bonus inside a fixed share of non-vendor operating costs for the next two quarters. Lean 20 to 25 percent. Base 25 to 30 percent. Growth 30 to 35 percent.

Auto step-up language  
“Base moves from Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 on the earliest of soft-launch gate, funding close, or revenue run-rate threshold. Bonus cap moves with the mode.”

---

## 5. Placement by capability and time in role
| Capability | 0 to 12 months | 12 to 36 months | 36 months plus |
|---|---|---|---|
| Foundational | Quartile 1 to low Quartile 2 | Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 | Quartile 2 |
| Proficient | Quartile 2 | Mid to high Quartile 2 | Low Quartile 3 |
| Expert | Quartile 2 to low Quartile 3 | Quartile 3 | High Quartile 3 to Quartile 4 |

This matrix is your first filter. Use it, then adjust inside a quartile for scope and scarcity with a short written note.

---

## 6. Role scorecards and bonus mathematics
All roles follow one rule.  
Bonus payout equals Target bonus multiplied by the Weighted KPI score and is capped by mode.

CEO scorecard  
Funding or revenue gate 40 percent. Delivery gates 30 percent. Senior hiring and team health 20 percent. Board reporting hygiene 10 percent.

Worked example  
Target bonus 35 percent. Scores 0.9, 0.8, 0.7, 1.0 respectively. Weighted KPI score equals 0.86. Payout equals 30.1 percent of base. This is within the Base mode cap.

Create matching four-line scorecards for COO, CFO, CTO, CPO and Executive Producer that reflect your current plan. Keep weights visible in offer letters.

---

## 7. Equity bands and founder control
Grant bands  
CEO 2.0 to 5.0 percent. CTO, CFO, COO, CPO 0.25 to 1.00 percent. Executive Producer 0.10 to 0.30 percent. Vesting four years with a one-year cliff. Change of control uses double-trigger acceleration.

Governance  
No grant above band without a written case that shows scarcity proof, value proof, control impact and ESOP sufficiency. Option pool starts at 10 to 15 percent unallocated and is refreshed at financing or when signed hiring plans require it. Pool increases are negotiated pre-money so all holders dilute pro rata.

Control lines to hold  
Seed through close: CEO at least 50.1 percent post-transaction or equivalent effective control through the board. Through Series A: CEO at least 33.4 percent with board control safeguards and participation rights.

Fast control test  
If Investors take p percent and the ESOP is e percent post-round, a founder’s new percentage equals the founder’s pre-round percentage multiplied by 1 minus p minus e. Use this before signing a term sheet and before any out-of-band equity grant.

---

## 8. Offer construction that anyone on the team can operate
1. Select the London or Athens table.  
2. Pick the runway mode and set the bonus cap.  
3. Place the candidate in a quartile using capability and time in role.  
4. Choose a specific number inside that quartile.  
5. Set the bonus target from the scorecard, apply the cap, and add the equity grant from the band.  
6. Run five checks and note them on the cover sheet.  
   Parity with peers. Non-inversion against the highest functional leader in the same city. Budget envelope. Control test. FX display rule respected.  
7. For Athens, insert the standard sentence about Christmas, Easter and leave allowances and show the monthly split in the letter.

## 11. Athens Total Cost to Company example
Annualised base €180,000.  
If paid as a 14-month practice: monthly base €12,857 and two extra half-months for Easter and leave, one extra full month for Christmas.

COO, Athens, Lean mode with an automatic step  
“This role uses the Athens band. Given Lean runway we are placing base in Quartile 1 with an automatic step to Quartile 2 at the first soft-launch gate. The bonus is capped at 20 percent and tied to readiness and throughput. The contract states whether Christmas, Easter and leave allowances are included in the figure or paid separately.”

# Corrected document front matter and framing

## Couch Heroes  
### Executive Compensation Study and Guide  
UK and Greece, AA studio, pre-revenue

Prepared by an executive compensation advisor with CEO and COO review

### Purpose
Provide the leadership of Couch Heroes with a practical, defensible framework to set base pay, bonus, and equity for C-level roles in London and Athens. The guide translates current 2025 market signals into quartile pay bands by role and city, aligns decisions to financial position, and protects founder control while ensuring fair treatment across locations.

### How to use this guide
1. Select the London or Athens band for the employing entity.  
2. Choose the current runway mode.  
3. Place the role in a pay quartile using the capability and time-in-role matrix.  
4. Set the bonus target from the role scorecard and apply the mode cap.  
5. Grant equity from the band. Run parity, non-inversion, budget, FX, and founder-control checks.

## Principles
- Cash and bonus are set by location. Equity is location-agnostic at the same level.  
- Quartiles provide room to place individuals without breaking internal parity.  
- Bonuses pay on delivery against short, weighted scorecards.  
- Equity bands keep offers competitive while controlling dilution.  
- Founder capital is recognised through appropriate instruments, not salary.  
- Offers are issued and paid in local currency. Alternate currency is shown in parentheses for comparison only.

## Method
- Ranges are anchored to current 2025 sources and normalised to local currency.  
- Quartiles are presented from the observed market range. Where a median is available, placement guidance references it. Where direct Athens data is limited, the row is labelled inferred for priority refresh.  
- Alternate currency figures follow a fixed FX snapshot for consistent internal comparison.

## Location fairness and Greek practice
- London pay reflects UK cost of labour and senior-talent competition.  
- Athens pay may use a 14-month practice in the private sector. Quote Athens offers as annualised figures and state whether Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are included in the annualised number or paid as separate instalments.  
- If a leader relocates between London and Athens, equity is unchanged. Cash moves to the new location band at the next review.

## Runway modes that adjust cash, bonus, and equity
| Mode | When to use | Base placement | Bonus cap | Equity stance |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Lean runway | Less than nine months of runway or pre-funding | Quartile 1 to low Quartile 2 | CEO 25 percent; other C-level 20 percent | Grants at the lower half of band; no off-cycle refresh |
| Base | Nine to eighteen months of runway or funding signed | Quartile 2 | CEO 35 percent; other C-level 25 percent | Grants mid-band; refresh at annual cycle |
| Growth | More than eighteen months of runway or live revenue | High Quartile 2 to Quartile 3 | CEO 40 percent; other C-level 30 percent | Grants at upper half for scarce roles with a written case |

Budget discipline  
Keep combined C-team base plus target bonus within a fixed share of non-vendor operating costs for the next two quarters: Lean 20–25 percent; Base 25–30 percent; Growth 30–35 percent.

Automatic step clause  
“Base moves from Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 on the earliest of soft-launch gate, funding close, or revenue run-rate threshold. The bonus cap moves with the mode.”

## Placement by capability and time in role
| Capability | 0 to 12 months | 12 to 36 months | 36 months plus |
|---|---|---|---|
| Foundational | Quartile 1 to low Quartile 2 | Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 | Quartile 2 |
| Proficient | Quartile 2 | Mid to high Quartile 2 | Low Quartile 3 |
| Expert | Quartile 2 to low Quartile 3 | Quartile 3 | High Quartile 3 to Quartile 4 |

Use this matrix to place roles, then adjust within the quartile for scope and scarcity with a short written note.

## Bonus design and worked example
Payout rule  
Bonus payout equals Target bonus multiplied by the Weighted KPI score, capped by mode.

CEO scorecard  
Funding or revenue gate 40 percent. Delivery gates 30 percent. Senior hiring and team health 20 percent. Board reporting hygiene 10 percent.

Worked example  
Target bonus 35 percent. Scores 0.9, 0.8, 0.7, 1.0. Weighted KPI score equals 0.86. Payout equals 30.1 percent of base, within the Base mode cap.

## Equity bands and founder control
Grant bands  
CEO 2.0–5.0 percent. CTO, CFO, COO, CPO 0.25–1.00 percent. Executive Producer 0.10–0.30 percent. Vesting four years with a one-year cliff. Change of control uses double-trigger acceleration.

Governance  
No grant above band without a written case covering scarcity, value, control impact, and ESOP sufficiency. Option pool starts at 10–15 percent unallocated and refreshes at financing or when signed hiring plans require it. Pool increases are negotiated pre-money so all holders dilute pro rata.

Control lines  
Seed: CEO at least 50.1 percent post-transaction, or equivalent effective control through the board. Through Series A: CEO at least 33.4 percent with board control safeguards and participation rights.

Control check  
If Investors take p percent and ESOP is e percent post-round, a founder’s new percentage equals the founder’s pre-round percentage multiplied by 1 − p − e. Run this check before agreeing terms or issuing any out-of-band grant.

## Offer construction
1. Select the London or Athens table.  
2. Choose the runway mode and set the bonus cap.  
3. Place the candidate in a quartile using the capability and time-in-role matrix.  
4. Choose a specific number within that quartile.  
5. Set the bonus target from the scorecard and add the equity grant from the band.  
6. Run five checks and record them: parity with peers, non-inversion against the highest functional leader in the same city, budget envelope, control check, FX display rule.  
7. For Athens, insert the allowances sentence and show the monthly split in the letter.

## Closing note
This document is intended for the leadership of Couch Heroes. It provides a consistent, transparent method to set compensation across London and Athens, linked to delivery and runway, with clear controls for parity and founder ownership.

# Couch Heroes  
## Executive Compensation Study and Guide  
UK and Greece, AA studio, pre-revenue

Prepared by an executive compensation advisor, with CEO and COO review

### Purpose
Provide the leadership of Couch Heroes with a clear, defensible method to set executive base pay, bonus and equity for London and Athens. The guide translates current 2025 market signals into four pay quartiles by role and location, introduces simple controls that reflect financial position, ensures fair treatment between the UK and Greece, and protects founder control.

### How to use this guide
1. Select the location band, London or Athens.  
2. Choose the runway mode for the next six months.  
3. Place the role in a pay quartile using the capability and time-in-role matrix.  
4. Set the bonus target from the role scorecard and apply the mode cap.  
5. Grant equity from the band, then complete the parity, non-inversion, budget, FX and control checks.

## 1. Principles
- Cash and bonus are location-anchored. Equity is location-agnostic for the same level.  
- Quartiles provide structured room to place individuals while maintaining internal parity.  
- Bonuses pay on measured delivery using short, weighted scorecards.  
- Equity bands keep offers competitive and guard against unintended dilution.  
- Offers are issued and paid in the local currency of contract. Alternate currency appears in parentheses for comparison only.  
- Founder capital is recognised through instruments, not salary.

## 2. Method
- Ranges are anchored to current 2025 sources and normalised to local currency.  
- Quartiles are shown as Q1 to Q4 across the observed market range. Where a median exists, placement guidance references it. Where a role lacks direct Athens data, the row is marked inferred and prioritised for refresh.  
- Alternate currency appears in parentheses. A fixed FX snapshot is used for internal comparisons.

## 3. Location fairness and Greek practice
- London reflects UK cost of labour and competition for senior talent.  
- Athens often uses a 14-month practice in the private sector. Quote Athens offers as annualised figures and state whether Christmas, Easter and leave allowances are included in the annualised base or paid as separate instalments.  
- If an executive relocates between cities, equity is unchanged. Cash moves to the new location band at the next review.

## 4. Runway modes that adjust cash, bonus and equity
| Mode | When to use | Base placement | Bonus cap | Equity stance |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Lean runway | Fewer than nine months of runway or pre-funding | Quartile 1 to low Quartile 2 | CEO 25 percent, other C-level 20 percent | Grants in the lower half of band, no mid-cycle refresh |
| Base | Nine to eighteen months of runway or funding signed | Quartile 2 | CEO 35 percent, other C-level 25 percent | Grants mid-band, refresh at annual cycle |
| Growth | More than eighteen months of runway or live revenue | High Quartile 2 to Quartile 3 | CEO 40 percent, other C-level 30 percent | Grants in the upper half for scarce roles, with a written case |

Budget discipline  
Keep combined C-team base plus target bonus within a fixed share of non-vendor operating costs for the next two quarters: Lean 20–25 percent, Base 25–30 percent, Growth 30–35 percent.

Automatic progression clause  
“Base progresses from Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 on the earliest of soft-launch gate, funding close, or revenue run-rate threshold. Bonus cap follows the active runway mode.”

## 5. Placement by capability and time in role
| Capability | 0 to 12 months | 12 to 36 months | 36 months plus |
|---|---|---|---|
| Foundational | Quartile 1 to low Quartile 2 | Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 | Quartile 2 |
| Proficient | Quartile 2 | Mid to high Quartile 2 | Low Quartile 3 |
| Expert | Quartile 2 to low Quartile 3 | Quartile 3 | High Quartile 3 to Quartile 4 |

## 6. Role scorecards and bonus calculation
Rule  
Bonus payout equals Target bonus multiplied by the Weighted KPI score, capped by the runway mode.

Example, CEO scorecard  
Funding or revenue gate 40 percent, delivery gates 30 percent, senior hiring and team health 20 percent, board reporting quality and timeliness 10 percent.

Worked calculation  
Target bonus 35 percent. Scores 0.9, 0.8, 0.7, 1.0 respectively. Weighted KPI score 0.86. Payout 30.1 percent of base, within the Base-mode cap.

Create matching four-line scorecards for COO, CFO, CTO, CPO and Executive Producer aligned to the current plan.

## 7. Equity bands and control safeguards
Grant bands  
CEO 2.0–5.0 percent. CTO, CFO, COO, CPO 0.25–1.00 percent. Executive Producer 0.10–0.30 percent. Vesting four years with a one-year cliff. Change of control uses double-trigger acceleration.

Approval rules  
No grant above band without a written case showing evidence of scarcity, business value, control impact and ESOP sufficiency. Option pool starts at 10–15 percent unallocated and is refreshed at financing or when signed hiring plans require it. Pool increases are negotiated pre-money so all holders dilute pro rata.

Control lines to hold  
At Seed, CEO at least 50.1 percent post-transaction, or equivalent effective control through the board. Through Series A, CEO at least 33.4 percent with board control safeguards and participation rights.

Quick control test  
If investors take p percent and the ESOP is e percent post-round, a founder’s post-round percentage equals the founder’s pre-round percentage multiplied by 1 minus p minus e.

## 8. Offer construction for the executive team
1. Select the London or Athens table.  
2. Choose the runway mode and note the bonus cap.  
3. Place the candidate in a quartile using capability and time in role.  
4. Select a specific figure within that quartile.  
5. Set the bonus target from the scorecard and apply the cap.  
6. Add the equity grant from the band.  
7. Complete five checks and record them: parity with peers, non-inversion against the highest functional leader in the same city, budget envelope, control test, FX display rule.  
8. For Athens, include the allowances sentence and show the monthly split in the letter.

# Couch Heroes Leadership Compensation Guide 2025  
**Scope:** Chief, VP, and Director level pay architecture for London and Athens. Focused on an AA, pre-revenue studio with AAA ambition.  
**Audience:** Couch Heroes leadership.  
**Outcome:** A clear, defensible method to set base, bonus, and equity for senior and executive roles in the UK and Greece, with cross-border fairness and founder-control preserved.

---

## 1) How to use this guide in 5 steps

1. **Pick the right city grid** (London or Athens) and the **right role**.  
2. Choose a **quartile band** based on company stage and cash position:  
   - Q1 = conservative cash posture, early proof phase  
   - Q2 = typical AA pre-revenue posture  
   - Q3 = confident ramp to beta with runway  
   - Q4 = scarce talent or time-critical hire  
3. Apply **skill/tenure calibration** to nudge inside the chosen quartile:  
   - First-time in seat = lower half of the quartile  
   - Seasoned operator = mid of the quartile  
   - Scale veteran = upper half of the quartile  
4. Add **bonus target** and **equity** from Sections 4 and 5.  
5. For Greece, convert to a **14-month payroll** presentation if you follow local practice, and confirm total on-target earnings parity with the UK counterpart. citeturn1search20turn1search22turn1search23

**FX snapshot for cross-checking:** ECB reference, 27 Oct 2025, 1 EUR ≈ 0.8721 GBP. Use for parentheses conversions below. citeturn1search18

---

## 2) Sources and method (what’s in, what’s out)

- **Primary London benchmarks (2025):**  
  CTO £130k–£160k (Morgan McKinley) ; CPO £190k–£230k (Morgan McKinley) ; CFO broader market range £120k–£250k (Morgan McKinley calculator) ; Executive Producer London £70k–£95k (TechNET Immersive 2025). citeturn0search0turn6search8turn5search8turn5search2

## 4) Bonus targets (pre-revenue posture, on-target)

- CEO: 0–20 percent (defer or equity-settle if cash is tight)  
- COO: 10–20 percent  
- CFO: 10–25 percent  
- CTO: 10–20 percent  
- CPO: 10–20 percent  
- Executive Producer: 10–15 percent

Post-revenue, lift targets one notch and tie to OTE measures such as live-ops EBIT contribution, release milestones, and retention goals.

---

## 5) Equity framework that protects control and stays fair

- **ESOP pool:** 10 percent at seed-close, refresh to 15 percent before a larger round.  
- **Typical new-hire grants:**  
  - CFO/COO/CTO/CPO: 0.8–2.0 percent, 4-year vest, 1-year cliff  
  - VP: 0.3–1.0 percent  
  - Director: 0.15–0.6 percent  
- **Founder control:** keep voting structure so the CEO retains majority voting after pool expansions and early hires. Add standard founder vesting and double-trigger acceleration for key leaders at acquisition.

These percentages are consistent with UK startup practice and AA studio norms where base is moderated and equity compensates for risk. Use the lower half of bands while pre-revenue; step toward mid after financing or strong market traction. citeturn5search1

---

## 6) Skill and tenure calibration (how to move inside a quartile)

- **First-time in seat:** select the lower half of the chosen quartile.  
- **Seasoned operator:** select the mid of the quartile.  
- **Scale veteran (shipped multiple AA/AAA, or built functions at scale):** upper half of the quartile.  

Calibration signals include shipped titles at similar scale, breadth of P&L accountability, and prior team size. For Athens, also factor leadership in distributed teams and English-language external stakeholder work.

---

## 7) Cross-border parity and Greek 14-month pay

Greece commonly uses a 14-month pay pattern: one month at Christmas, half a month at Easter, and half a month for holiday, on top of 12 monthly payments. That changes how offers are presented but not total on-target earnings. Maintain parity by equalising **annual OTE**, not the monthly cheque. If you adopt 14-month presentation in Athens, express London’s package as an annual figure with the same OTE and show the monthly breakdown separately. citeturn1search20turn1search22turn1search23

---

## 8) Stage modifiers for an AA pre-revenue studio

- **Cash-preserve setting:** pick Q1 for base, cut cash bonus to the floor of the band, shift value into equity with vesting.  
- **Runway-secure setting:** pick Q2 for base and mid bonus.  
- **Critical hire or schedule compression:** pick Q3–Q4 for base and bonus, but offset with stricter milestones and vesting cliffs.

---

### Example A: CEO in London, AA pre-revenue, runway adequate  
- **Base:** Q2 midpoint ≈ £230k (EUR ≈ £275k)

- **Equity:** no new founder grant required; protect majority voting while expanding ESOP to 10 percent  
- **Rationale:** CEO base sits above London CTO/CPO medians, aligned to role accountability and investor optics. citeturn0search0turn6search8

### Example B: CTO in Athens, pre-revenue, critical hire  
- **Base:** Q3 ≈ €100k–€108k (GBP ≈ £87k–£95k) presented as 14-month payroll  
- **Bonus target:** 15 percent  
- **Equity:** 1.0 percent, 4-year vest, 1-year cliff  
- **Rationale:** market-aligned to ERI Athens CTO, with equity making up for pre-revenue risk, and OTE parity maintained to the London peer. citeturn2search12turn1search20

## 10) Offer construction checklist

- Select role and city table, choose quartile by stage.  
- Calibrate for skill and tenure.  
- Convert and present correctly for 12-month (UK) vs 14-month (Greece) formats.  
- Add bonus target and clear milestone gates.  
- Add equity within ranges and confirm post-grant founder voting control.  
- Record rationale and sources in the offer file.

## 11) One-page calculator spec (for your spreadsheet)

**Inputs:** Role, City, Quartile, Skill/Tenure level, Bonus target, Equity percent, FX rate, Greece 14-month flag.  
**Calcs:**  
- Base GBP↔EUR using ECB snapshot  
- Monthly presentation by country format (12 or 14)  
- Bonus at target and at threshold  
- Equity grant value at latest 409A-style internal valuation  
- OTE and cash burn impact by hire

## What to fix to reach 10/10 on readability

1) **Replace stacked bullets with short paragraphs.**  
   Each section should open with a one-sentence purpose, a two-to-three sentence explanation, then a compact table if needed.

2) **Add connective transitions.**  
   Use bridging lines such as “What this means for Couch Heroes,” “How to apply this on Monday,” and “Common failure modes to avoid.”

3) **Show, do not list.**  
   One worked offer per city, written as a mini narrative, beats four bullets. Keep the numbers; explain why they were chosen.

4) **Define terms once.**  
   Explain quartiles, runway modes, and Greek allowances in plain English, then use them consistently.

5) **Move governance checks into a single closing checklist.**  
   Put the five checks on one page so a leader can tick through them in order.

6) **Strip internal jargon.**  
   Replace “signals,” “out-of-band,” and “hygiene” with “market ranges,” “above-band,” and “quality and timeliness.”

## Sample rewrite, as it should read in the white paper

**Runway modes, and why they matter now**  
Couch Heroes is pre-revenue, so cash discipline is central. Runway modes link pay to affordability over the next six months. In Lean mode, place executives in Quartile 1, cap bonuses at 20 to 25 percent, and keep equity grants in the lower half of the band. In Base mode, move to Quartile 2 with standard caps. In Growth mode, where runway exceeds eighteen months or live revenue is established, you can place scarce roles higher, but record the business case and run the control test before you issue the offer. This keeps pay decisions consistent with the studio’s financial position and prevents drift.

**How to place an offer, end to end**  
Select the London or Athens table. Choose the current runway mode. Use the capability and time-in-role matrix to pick a quartile. Set a specific figure inside that quartile, add the bonus target from the role scorecard, then add the equity grant from the band. Finish with five checks: parity, non-inversion, budget envelope, founder-control, and the FX display rule. For Athens, state clearly whether Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are included in the annualised figure or paid as separate instalments, and show the monthly breakdown either way.

---

## Two worked offers, written for a human reader

**CEO, London, Base mode**  
The CEO band in London runs from £200,000 to £260,000, shown with the euro equivalent in parentheses for board comparison. Given the scope and track record, place the CEO in Quartile 2 at £210,000. Set a 35 percent target bonus with weights on funding, delivery gates, team health, and reporting quality. Equity remains within the CEO band and does not require a new founder grant at this stage. This placement keeps the CEO above the highest functional median, fits inside the Base-mode budget envelope, and passes the control test.

**COO, Athens, Lean mode with progression**  
Use the Athens COO band. Start at Quartile 1 given Lean mode and write an automatic progression to Quartile 2 at the first soft-launch gate. Set the bonus cap at 20 percent with readiness and throughput as the primary measures. Present the offer in annual terms and add the standard sentence explaining whether Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are included in the annualised figure or paid as separate instalments. Equity sits in the lower half of the COO band, which preserves the option pool and keeps the CEO above the control line.

Here is a clean, client-grade writing pass. It keeps all of the structure and control you asked for, but reads like a professional white paper addressed to the leadership of Couch Heroes, not a bundle of notes.

# Couch Heroes Leadership Compensation Guide 2025  
Scope: Chief, VP, and Director level pay architecture for London and Athens.  
Context: AA, pre-revenue studio with AAA ambition.  
Audience: the leadership of Couch Heroes.

## 1. Purpose and what success looks like
This guide gives the leadership a clear, defensible way to set executive base pay, bonus, and equity in London and Athens. It explains how to use market quartiles without creating pay inversions, how to keep cash aligned to the studio’s financial position, and how to treat London and Athens fairly while preserving founder control. If the guide works as intended, an executive can price an offer in minutes, explain the choice in plain language, and show it passes budget and cap table checks.

## 2. How to use this guide
Begin by selecting the correct city band for the employing entity, London or Athens. Choose the studio’s current posture for the next six months, which this guide calls the runway mode. Place the role into a quartile using the capability and time-in-role matrix, then set bonus and equity from the relevant sections. Finish by running five checks in order: peer parity, non-inversion within the city, budget envelope, founder control, and the currency display rule. For Athens, include the standard allowances sentence and show the monthly presentation as required by local practice.

## 3. Principles that hold this together
Cash and bonus are set by location to reflect the cost of labour and competition for talent. Equity is location-agnostic at the same level so London and Athens leaders are treated fairly on ownership. Quartiles provide structured room to place individuals without losing parity. Bonuses pay on measured delivery using short, weighted scorecards. Equity bands keep offers competitive and prevent unintended dilution. Offers are issued and paid in the local currency of contract, with the alternate currency shown in parentheses for comparison.

## 4. Method and confidence
Ranges are anchored to current 2025 sources and normalised to local currency. Where a robust market median exists, placement guidance references it. Where Athens games-specific data are thin for a particular role, the line is marked as a proxy and flagged for early refresh. Tables display local currency first and the alternate currency in parentheses so London and Athens can be compared at a glance.

## 5. Runway modes explained
Couch Heroes is pre-revenue, so affordability matters. Runway modes link pay choices to the next six months of cash outlook.

In Lean mode, select Quartile 1 or the lower half of Quartile 2, cap bonuses at the low end, and keep equity in the lower half of the band. In Base mode, use Quartile 2 with standard caps. In Growth mode, where runway is comfortable or live revenue is established, scarce roles can be placed higher, but record the business case and run the founder control test before issuing the offer.

Include an automatic progression clause in any Lean placement. Base pay moves from Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 at the earliest of a soft-launch gate, a funding close, or an agreed revenue threshold. The bonus cap follows the active runway mode.

## 6. Placing individuals fairly
Use the capability and time-in-role matrix as your first filter. A first-time executive sits in the lower half of the chosen quartile. A seasoned operator sits near the middle. A scale veteran with multiple shipped titles or function build-outs sits in the upper half. Adjust inside the quartile for scope and scarcity, then write a one-line rationale that would make sense to a board member reading it six months later.

### Capability and time-in-role matrix
| Capability | 0 to 12 months | 12 to 36 months | 36 months plus |
|---|---|---|---|
| Foundational | Q1 to low Q2 | Q1 to Q2 | Q2 |
| Proficient | Q2 | Mid to high Q2 | Low Q3 |
| Expert | Q2 to low Q3 | Q3 | High Q3 to Q4 |

## 7. London ranges with alternate currency in parentheses
Figures are base salary quartiles. GBP appears first with the EUR equivalent in parentheses.

| Role | Q1 | Q2 | Q3 | Q4 |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Chief Executive Officer | £200,000–£215,000 (EUR 229,400–246,600) | £215,000–£230,000 (EUR 246,600–263,800) | £230,000–£245,000 (EUR 263,800–281,000) | £245,000–£260,000 (EUR 281,000–298,200) |
| Chief Operating Officer | £120,000–£130,000 (EUR 137,600–149,100) | £130,000–£140,000 (EUR 149,100–160,600) | £140,000–£150,000 (EUR 160,600–172,000) | £150,000–£160,000 (EUR 172,000–183,500) |
| Chief Financial Officer | £120,000–£152,500 (EUR 137,600–174,900) | £152,500–£185,000 (EUR 174,900–212,200) | £185,000–£217,500 (EUR 212,200–249,500) | £217,500–£250,000 (EUR 249,500–286,700) |

The CEO band is set as a policy anchor above the highest functional medians to prevent accidental role inversion at AA stage.

## 8. Athens ranges with alternate currency in parentheses
Figures are base salary quartiles. EUR appears first with the GBP equivalent in parentheses. Athens often uses a 14-month pay pattern. Offers should be quoted on an annualised basis, with the contract stating whether Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are included in the annualised number or paid as separate instalments.

## 9. The Greek 14-month presentation made simple
Total on-target earnings are the anchor. If the annualised base is €180,000 and the 14-month pattern is in use, the monthly cheque is €12,857 with an extra month at Christmas and two half-months at Easter and leave. If you equalise to 12 months, the monthly amount is €15,000. The total for the year is the same. State which method applies in the offer and show the split.

## 10. Bonus design that pays on delivery
Every role uses the same formula. Bonus payout equals the target bonus multiplied by the weighted KPI score, subject to the runway mode cap. Keep scorecards short and auditable.

A CEO scorecard can weight funding or revenue gates at forty percent, delivery gates at thirty percent, senior hiring and team health at twenty percent, and reporting quality at ten percent. If the target is thirty five percent and the weighted KPI score calculates to 0.86, the payout is 30.1 percent of base, which is within the Base mode cap. COO, CFO, CTO, CPO, and Executive Producer should follow the same four-line pattern, each tied to the plan they are accountable to.

## 11. Equity bands with founder control safeguards
Equity is where fairness and control meet. Grant bands keep offers consistent: CEO typically sits between 2.0 and 5.0 percent. CTO, CFO, COO, and CPO sit between 0.25 and 1.00 percent. Executive Producer sits between 0.10 and 0.30 percent. Vesting is four years with a one-year cliff. Change of control should use double-trigger acceleration only.

No above-band grant should be made without a short written case covering scarcity, business value, control impact, and whether the option pool remains sufficient. Plan for a ten percent pool at seed close and refresh to fifteen percent only when a signed hiring plan requires it. Negotiate pool increases pre-money so all existing holders dilute proportionally.

Hold two control lines. At seed, the CEO should remain at least 50.1 percent post-transaction, or retain equivalent effective control through the board. Through Series A, the CEO should remain at least 33.4 percent with board safeguards and participation rights. A simple control test helps: if investors will hold p percent post-round and the option pool is e percent post-round, multiply the founder’s pre-round percentage by one minus p minus e to estimate the post-round percentage before any participation.

## 12. Two worked offers you can reuse
**CEO, London, Base mode**. The CEO band runs from £200,000 to £260,000 with the euro equivalent in parentheses. Given scope and track record, place the CEO in Quartile 2 at £210,000. Set a thirty five percent target bonus with weights on funding, delivery gates, team health, and reporting quality. Equity remains within the CEO band and does not require a new founder grant at this stage. This placement keeps the CEO above the highest functional median, fits the Base mode budget envelope, and passes the control test.

**COO, Athens, Lean mode with progression**. Use the Athens COO band. Start at Quartile 1 given Lean mode and write an automatic progression to Quartile 2 at the first soft-launch gate or funding close. Cap the bonus at twenty percent with readiness and throughput as the primary measures. Present the offer in annual terms and include the standard sentence explaining whether Christmas, Easter, and leave allowances are included in the figure or paid separately. Equity sits in the lower half of the COO band, preserving the pool and keeping the CEO above the control line.

## 13. Offer construction and governance in one place
Select the role and city table and choose the quartile that matches the runway mode. Calibrate for capability and time in role, then select a specific figure within the quartile. Add the bonus target from the role scorecard and apply the cap for the mode. Add the equity grant from the band. Confirm five checks and record them with the offer: parity with peers, non-inversion against the highest functional leader in the same city, budget envelope by mode, founder control test, and the currency rule. For Athens, include the allowances sentence and show the monthly split.

## 14. Evidence and refresh
Maintain a one-page table per role and city with the exact source, the date it was captured, whether the row is observed or a proxy, a confidence tag, and the next refresh date. Reconfirm London annually and Athens at the same cadence or when a financing event changes the plan. Replace the Athens CPO proxy first when games-specific data become available.

# Couch Heroes Leadership Compensation Guide 2025  
Scope: Chief, VP, and Director level pay architecture for London and Athens.  
Context: AA, pre-revenue studio with AAA ambition.  
Audience: the leadership of Couch Heroes.

## 1. Purpose and how to use this
This guide gives the leadership a clear, defensible method to set executive base pay, bonus, and equity in London and Athens. It balances three factors for every decision: role, cost of labour by location, and demonstrated skill in role. Read the range tables, choose a quartile that matches the individual’s capability, apply the target bonus and equity from the companion tables, then confirm affordability and cap table impact before issuing the offer.

## 2. Principles
- Cash and bonus are location-anchored. Equity is location-agnostic at the same level so London and Athens leaders are treated fairly on ownership.  
- Quartiles provide structured room to place individuals without losing parity.  
- Bonuses pay on measured delivery using short, weighted scorecards.  
- Equity bands keep offers competitive and prevent unintended dilution.  
- Offers are issued and paid in the local currency of contract, with the alternate currency shown in parentheses for comparison.

|---|---|---|---|

| Proficient | Quartile 2 | Middle to upper half of Quartile 2 | Lower half of Quartile 3 |
| Expert | Quartile 2 to lower half of Quartile 3 | Quartile 3 | Upper half of Quartile 3 to Quartile 4 |

## 8. Affordability and control checks before you sign
- **Affordability:** confirm total leadership cash spend fits the next two quarters of non-vendor operating cost you are prepared to allocate.  
- **Parity:** confirm the placement is consistent with peers at the same level and city.  
- **Non-inversion:** confirm the CEO sits above the highest functional median in the same city.  
- **Equity pool:** confirm the ESOP remains sufficient after grants and refreshes.  
- **Founder control:** if investors will hold p percent post round and the ESOP will be e percent post round, a founder’s post percentage is the founder’s pre-round percentage multiplied by 1 minus p minus e. Use this to confirm the CEO remains above the agreed control line.

# Couch Heroes Leadership Compensation Guide 2025

## Executive summary
This guide sets out how Couch Heroes will determine executive compensation in London and Athens for Chief, Vice-President, and Director roles in an AA, pre-revenue studio with AAA ambition. The approach balances three things. First, the realities of each role’s scope and accountability. Second, the cost of labour by location. Third, proven capability and time in seat. Base pay, annual bonus, and equity are expressed in quartiles so leaders can recognise strength without breaking internal parity. London and Athens are treated fairly by anchoring cash to location while keeping equity location-agnostic. Currency is shown in the local contract currency with the alternate in parentheses for simple comparison. Greek 14-month pay practice is explained so there is no confusion when making offers.

## 1. How decisions are made
Compensation is set by combining role, location, and demonstrated skill. Begin with the correct city table. For London, base salary quartiles are shown in pounds with euros in parentheses. For Athens, base salary quartiles are shown in euros with pounds in parentheses. Select a quartile that reflects the executive’s capability and time in role, not just job title. A first-time leader in the seat belongs in the lower half of the chosen quartile, an experienced operator belongs near the middle, and a scale veteran who has delivered multiple titles or built functions at size belongs in the upper half. Record a one-line rationale for each placement so the decision remains defensible at board review.

Quartiles are a control. They provide headroom to reward skill and scope without creating inversions where a functional head out-earns the Chief Executive Officer or equivalent anomalies. The Chief Executive Officer quartiles are therefore set as a policy anchor above the highest functional medians at AA stage. Annual bonus targets and equity grants use matching quartiles, which keeps the overall package coherent and reduces the risk of over-correcting with any single element.

## 3. Annual bonus design

Annual bonus targets are expressed as a percentage of base salary and are aligned across locations so incentives remain consistent. Each role has a short, weighted scorecard tied to measurable outcomes. The bonus payout is simply the target percentage multiplied by the weighted KPI score, with weights disclosed in the offer letter so there is no ambiguity at year end.

| Role | Quartile 1 | Quartile 2 | Quartile 3 | Quartile 4 |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Chief Executive Officer | 10%–20% | 20%–30% | 30%–35% | 35%–40% |
| Chief Operating Officer | 10%–15% | 15%–20% | 20%–25% | 25%–30% |
| Chief Financial Officer | 10%–15% | 15%–20% | 20%–25% | 25%–30% |
| Chief Technology Officer | 10%–15% | 15%–20% | 20%–25% | 25%–30% |
| Chief Product Officer | 10%–15% | 15%–20% | 20%–25% | 25%–30% |
| Executive Producer | 10%–12% | 12%–14% | 14%–15% | 15%–18% |

A brief note on design intent. For the Chief Executive Officer, heavier weight sits on funding or revenue gates, on-time delivery of key milestones, leadership hiring and team health, and reporting quality. For the Chief Operating Officer, readiness and throughput dominate. For the Chief Financial Officer, cash runway, audit quality, and forecast accuracy are central. The same logic applies to the Chief Technology Officer, Chief Product Officer, and Executive Producer, each aligned to outcomes they control.

## 4. Equity grant bands

Equity is expressed as a fully diluted percentage at grant. Vesting is four years with a one-year cliff. Equity is location-agnostic so that leaders in London and Athens are treated fairly on ownership. The table shows where typical grants should land by quartile.

| Role | Quartile 1 | Quartile 2 | Quartile 3 | Quartile 4 |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Chief Executive Officer | 2.00%–2.75% | 2.75%–3.50% | 3.50%–4.25% | 4.25%–5.00% |
| Chief Operating Officer | 0.25%–0.45% | 0.45%–0.65% | 0.65%–0.85% | 0.85%–1.00% |
| Chief Financial Officer | 0.25%–0.45% | 0.45%–0.65% | 0.65%–0.85% | 0.85%–1.00% |
| Chief Technology Officer | 0.25%–0.45% | 0.45%–0.65% | 0.65%–0.85% | 0.85%–1.00% |
| Chief Product Officer | 0.25%–0.45% | 0.45%–0.65% | 0.65%–0.85% | 0.85%–1.00% |
| Executive Producer | 0.10%–0.15% | 0.15%–0.20% | 0.20%–0.25% | 0.25%–0.30% |

Governance is straightforward. Any grant above band requires a short written case covering scarcity, business value, impact on control, and whether the option pool remains sufficient. The option pool should begin around ten percent at seed and rise only when a signed hiring plan requires it. Pool increases should be negotiated pre-money so all holders dilute in proportion.

## 5. Cross-border consistency and Greek 14-month practice
Fairness across London and Athens depends on comparing like with like. London operates on a twelve-month payroll. Greece often presents pay over fourteen months in the private sector, with one extra month at Christmas and two half-months at Easter and holiday. Offers in Athens must be quoted as annualised figures and must state whether those allowances are included in the annualised base or paid as separate instalments. Parity is maintained by equalising annual on-target earnings, not by matching the monthly cheque. For example, an annualised base of €180,000 pays €12,857 per month on a fourteen-month pattern or €15,000 per month on a twelve-month pattern. The yearly total is the same. The contract must specify the method and the monthly presentation shown to the employee should match it.

## 6. Operating safeguards
Several checks keep decisions fair and affordable. Peer parity prevents unjustified gaps for the same role and quartile in the same city. A non-inversion check ensures the Chief Executive Officer remains above the highest functional median in that city. A budget check confirms that combined base pay and target bonuses for the leadership team fit inside the agreed share of operating costs. A founder control test confirms that planned grants and any option pool refresh do not push the Chief Executive Officer below the target ownership threshold for the stage. Finally, the currency rule requires that offers are issued and paid in the local currency of contract, with the alternate currency shown in parentheses for internal comparison only.

## 7. Evidence and refresh
The leadership team will maintain a simple evidence table alongside this guide. For each role and city, note the named source, the date it was captured, whether the line is directly observed or a proxy, the confidence level, and the next refresh date. London should be reconfirmed annually. Athens should be reconfirmed on the same cadence or at a financing event that changes the plan. The Athens Chief Product Officer line is the current priority for refresh when reliable games-specific data become available.

## 8. Closing note
This guide is written to be used, not debated. It gives the leadership of Couch Heroes a consistent way to recognise role scope, respect location realities, and reward proven capability, while keeping equity fair and founder control intact. If an exception is required, document it briefly and keep the evidence with the offer so it can be understood later without re-litigation.

# Couch Heroes Leadership Compensation Guide 2025

## Executive summary
This guide sets out how the leadership of Couch Heroes will determine executive compensation in London and Athens for Chief, Vice-President, and Director roles in an AA, pre-revenue studio with AAA ambition. The approach balances three elements. First, the scope and accountability of each role. Second, the cost of labour by location. Third, demonstrated capability and time in the seat. Base pay, annual bonus, and equity are expressed in quartiles so the team can recognise strength without breaking internal parity. London and Athens are treated fairly by anchoring cash to location and keeping equity location-agnostic. Currency is shown in the local contract currency with the alternate in parentheses for clarity. Greek 14-month pay practice is explained so offers are unambiguous.

## 1. How decisions are made
Compensation decisions combine role, location, and demonstrated skill. Begin with the correct city table. For London, base salary quartiles are shown in pounds with euros in parentheses. For Athens, base salary quartiles are shown in euros with pounds in parentheses. Select a quartile that reflects demonstrated capability and time in role, not just job title. A first-time leader in the seat belongs in the lower half of the chosen quartile, an experienced operator belongs near the middle, and a scale veteran with multiple shipped titles or function build-outs belongs in the upper half. Record a brief rationale for each placement so the decision remains clear at board review.

Quartiles provide structured headroom to recognise skill and scope without breaking internal parity. To avoid pay inversion, the Chief Executive Officer quartiles sit above the highest functional medians for AA studios. Annual bonus targets and equity grants use matching quartiles, which keeps the overall package coherent and avoids over-reliance on any single element.

|---|---|---|---|
| Foundational | Quartile 1 to the lower half of Quartile 2 | Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 | Quartile 2 |

You’re right to surface that explicitly. Here’s a clean section you can paste into the guide that locks founder control into the decision flow, with plain English rules, simple maths, and a couple of clear scenarios. It keeps the professional tone you asked for and avoids shorthand.

# Founder control and dilution framework

The leadership of Couch Heroes wants executive compensation to be fair without eroding the Chief Executive Officer’s control of the company. This section sets the control targets, the checks to run before each grant or financing, and practical ways to adjust terms so control is preserved while still hiring and rewarding senior talent.

## What “control” means in this guide

Control is defined as the Chief Executive Officer holding a voting majority of the company’s outstanding shares or effective voting control through the board. The preference order in this guide is:

1. Maintain at least 50.1 percent voting ownership after the seed round and through the next major financing if feasible for the plan.  
2. Where that level cannot be maintained because of financing size or pool expansion, lock effective control through board composition, voting agreements, and protective provisions, and set a minimum post-round ownership that is still credible for a founder Chief Executive Officer at an AA studio.

## Targets to hold

- Pre-seed to seed close: at least 50.1 percent voting ownership for the Chief Executive Officer.  
- Between seed and series A: aim to remain at or above 50.1 percent. If the funding plan requires a brief step below that level, the Chief Executive Officer should retain effective control through the board and voting agreements, and return to a majority as soon as practical.  
- Series A planning: do not proceed on terms that put the Chief Executive Officer below an agreed floor without explicit board approval and a written rationale. Set the floor before negotiations begin.

## The control test to run before any decision

Use the quick test whenever you plan a financing, a pool top-up, or a significant grant:

- Founder post-event percentage equals the founder pre-event percentage multiplied by one minus the investor post-money percentage minus the post-money option pool percentage.  
- If the result is below the agreed control line, rework one of the inputs before proceeding.

This simple test should be on the cover sheet of any term sheet or grant set for approval.

## Scenarios to make the maths concrete

**Scenario A: Seed with a modest pool and early grants**

Start with the Chief Executive Officer at 100 percent. Create a 10 percent employee option pool before any grants. The Chief Executive Officer now holds 90 percent. Grant 3 percent in total to early leaders from the pool. The Chief Executive Officer remains at 90 percent, the team holds 3 percent, and 7 percent remains unallocated in the pool. Raise a seed round for 20 percent of the company on a post-money basis. Everyone else scales by 0.8. The Chief Executive Officer becomes 72 percent, the team becomes 2.4 percent, the unallocated pool becomes 5.6 percent, and the seed investor holds 20 percent. The Chief Executive Officer remains in clear control.

**Scenario B: Series A with a large new investor and a pool top-up**

Continue from Scenario A. Pre-A, the Chief Executive Officer is 72 percent, the team is 2.4 percent, the pool is 5.6 percent, and the seed investor is 20 percent. Suppose a Series A investor proposes 25 percent post-money and asks to top the pool to 15 percent post-money. The dilution factor for all existing holders is one minus 0.25 minus the pool increase. The pool increase here is 9.4 percent to reach 15 percent. The factor is 0.656. The Chief Executive Officer would fall to about 47.2 percent, which fails the control line. Terms need to be adjusted.

## How to keep control and still hire well

When the control test fails, you have several levers. Use the lightest change that fixes the problem.

- Reduce the requested post-money percentage for the round and adjust the cheque size or valuation so that both the investor’s target return and your control line are respected.  
- Limit the pool refresh. If the current unallocated pool is sufficient for the next two signed hires, keep it and defer the top-up to the next round.  
- Shift value into cash for a scarce hire rather than lifting their equity quartile. Use a sign-on bonus or milestone bonus with clear gates.  
- Keep executive grants within the published quartiles and avoid above-band awards unless scarcity is proven and the control test still passes.  
- Where you need to grant near the top of a quartile for a time-critical hire, offset by lowering the grant for the next two leadership hires within the band.  
- Use non-voting option classes where your counsel supports it, or a voting agreement so that unexercised option holders do not erode practical control before exercise.  
- Maintain founder participation rights so the Chief Executive Officer can invest a small amount pro-rata to preserve percentage where appropriate.

## Governance that makes control explicit

Before you approve any round, pool change, or executive grant set, include a one-page summary with:

- The current capitalisation table.  
- The planned action and its inputs.  
- The quick control test result.  
- The Chief Executive Officer’s post-event percentage and whether it meets the agreed control line.  
- If it does not, the exact change made to bring it back into line, or the rationale for a temporary exception and the plan to return to the target.

## What this means in daily decisions

Hiring a Chief Technology Officer in Athens or a Chief Product Officer in London should never take the Chief Executive Officer below the control line if the grant sits within the equity quartile bands and is issued from an existing pool. Large movements happen when you combine a sizeable new investor, an aggressive pool refresh, and multiple above-band grants in the same quarter. Avoid stacking these. Sequence them, and run the control test after each step.

# Founder control and dilution

The leadership of Couch Heroes intends to compensate executives fairly while keeping the Chief Executive Officer in control of the company. Control in this guide means a simple voting majority of outstanding shares held by the Chief Executive Officer, or where equity temporarily dips, effective control through board composition and voting agreements.

## Control lines to hold
The primary control line is 50.1 percent voting ownership for the Chief Executive Officer. The studio should plan financings, option pool changes, and executive grants so that this line is maintained from pre-seed through seed and into the next major round. If a financing would push the Chief Executive Officer below 50.1 percent, do not proceed without an explicit board decision that sets a temporary exception, documents the rationale, and defines the steps and timing to return above 50.1 percent.

Where the leadership and investors agree that a short period below 50.1 percent is unavoidable, the Chief Executive Officer must retain effective control through a board majority, voting agreements that align common and option holders, and protective provisions that keep strategic control with the founders until the target ownership is restored.

## The control test to run every time
Before approving any financing, pool refresh, or set of senior grants, run this quick test:

Founder post-event percentage = Founder pre-event percentage × (1 − investor post-money percentage − post-money option pool percentage)

If the result is below 50.1 percent, rework one or more inputs. Typical adjustments are to reduce investor percentage, stage the cheque across milestones, limit the pool top-up, or move a scarce hire toward cash and bonus rather than the top of the equity band.

## Practical ways to preserve control while hiring well
Keep executive grants inside the published quartiles. Reserve above-band grants for proven scarcity with a short written case and only if the control test still passes. Favour cash and milestone bonuses for time-critical hires rather than lifting equity beyond the band. Do not combine a large pool refresh with multiple senior grants and a new round in the same quarter. Sequence them and run the control test after each step.

When refreshing the option pool, raise it only when a signed hiring plan requires it. Negotiate any pool increase on a pre-money basis so all existing holders dilute proportionally. Where counsel supports it, use non-voting option classes so unexercised options do not weaken practical control before exercise. Retain founder participation rights so the Chief Executive Officer can invest pro-rata in a round if needed to keep ownership above the line.

## Two concise scenarios

Seed with moderate hiring  
Start at 100 percent. Create a 10 percent option pool before any grants. The Chief Executive Officer now holds 90 percent. Grant 3 percent to early leaders from the pool. Raise a seed round for 20 percent post-money. All existing holders scale by 0.8. The Chief Executive Officer becomes 72 percent, the team becomes 2.4 percent, the remaining pool is 5.6 percent, and the investor holds 20 percent. Control is intact.

Series A proposal that would break control  
From the prior state, a new investor asks for 25 percent post-money and a pool top-up to 15 percent post-money. The dilution factor for all existing holders would be 1 − 0.25 − 0.094 = 0.656. The Chief Executive Officer would fall to about 47.2 percent, which fails the control line. Changes required include reducing investor percentage, staging funds against milestones, or limiting the pool refresh.

## Where this sits in the decision flow
This control section sits alongside the equity tables. The control test is added to the offer and financing cover sheet. No senior grant set, pool change, or term sheet proceeds to signature without a passing control test or a documented and time-bound temporary exception approved by the board.

### Governance checklist update
Add two items to the existing checklist:
- Control test result recorded with founder post-event percentage. Pass or temporary exception noted with owner and date.  
- If below 50.1 percent, the written plan to return above 50.1 percent is attached, with the steps and target timing.

# Founder control plan

## Purpose
Protect the Chief Executive Officer’s control while paying senior leaders fairly and keeping the option pool healthy. Control can be economic, voting, or both. This plan gives thresholds, maths, and governance so decisions are consistent across London and Athens.

## What “control” means in practice
- **Economic control** means the Chief Executive Officer holds more than 50 percent of the fully diluted ordinary shares.
- **Voting control** means the Chief Executive Officer can carry or block board and shareholder decisions under the company’s constitution, even if economic ownership dips below 50 percent. This is achieved with board composition, reserved matters, voting agreements, or dual-class voting where counsel confirms it is appropriate.

The studio should aim for economic control at seed. If that is not practical because of round size or pool needs, maintain voting control with clear safeguards and target a strong economic position that trends back up after growth milestones.

## Control thresholds by stage
These are policy lines for Couch Heroes. They guide round design and equity grants.

- **Pre-seed and seed:** Chief Executive Officer at least 50.1 percent post-transaction or equivalent voting control with board safeguards.
- **Through Series A:** Chief Executive Officer at least 33.4 percent economic ownership with voting control safeguards and participation rights.
- **Beyond Series A:** Maintain voting control and a clear path to restore economic percentage through growth, buybacks when appropriate, or reduced pool refresh after hiring peaks.

## The quick control test you can run on a call
If investors will hold **p percent** post-round and the option pool target is **e percent** post-round, a simple conservative estimate of the Chief Executive Officer’s post-round percentage is:

> Chief Executive Officer post ≈ Chief Executive Officer pre × (1 − p − e)

If the result is below the control line for the stage, reduce the round size, reduce the pool target, or add voting protections before you proceed.

## Worked control scenarios
These examples show how investor stake and pool size interact with a founder’s pre-round position. They are illustrative only. Your lawyer must confirm the exact mechanics for each round.

### Scenario A: Control preserved at seed
- **Pre-round:** Chief Executive Officer 70 percent. Chief Operating Officer 15 percent. Angels 5 percent. Option pool 10 percent.
- **Round ask:** Investor 15 percent post. Pool target 10 percent post.
- **Quick test:** 70 percent × (1 − 0.15 − 0.10) = 70 percent × 0.75 = **52.5 percent**.
- **Result:** Economic control preserved. Document board and reserved matters so voting control also holds.

### Scenario B: Control lost without safeguards
- **Pre-round:** Chief Executive Officer 60 percent. Chief Operating Officer 15 percent. Angels 15 percent. Option pool 10 percent.
- **Round ask:** Investor 20 percent post. Pool target 15 percent post.
- **Quick test:** 60 percent × (1 − 0.20 − 0.15) = 60 percent × 0.65 = **39.0 percent**.
- **Result:** Economic control lost. To proceed safely, reduce investor stake, reduce pool target, or add voting control mechanisms before signing.

### Scenario C: Voting control used where economics dip
- **Pre-round:** Chief Executive Officer 58 percent. Others 27 percent. Option pool 15 percent.
- **Round ask:** Investor 22 percent post. Pool target held at 15 percent.
- **Quick test:** 58 percent × (1 − 0.22 − 0.15) = 58 percent × 0.63 = **36.5 percent**.
- **Mitigation:** Retain a board majority through composition, use reserved matters for new share issues, option pool increases, debt, and M&A, and set founder participation rights. Document these before term-sheet signature.

## Equity and grant policy that supports control
- **Location neutrality:** Equity grants are the same for London and Athens at the same level so ownership is fair and transparent.
- **Grant bands:** Use the equity quartiles already defined in the guide. Stay inside the band unless a short written case proves scarcity and value.
- **Pool sizing:** Start at 10 percent fully diluted at seed. Refresh only against signed hiring plans. Target 10 to 12 percent between rounds. Avoid automatic refresh to 15 percent unless the plan demands it.
- **Above-band grants:** Require a written case that shows role criticality, evidence of scarcity, business value added, control impact, and pool sufficiency. File the case with the board approval.
- **Founder grants:** Avoid new founder equity grants post-formation. Recognise founder capital through instruments such as loans or advisory fees, not through repeated equity awards.

## Round design and board safeguards
- **Pre-money pool negotiation:** Increase the pool pre-money if required so that new investors dilute alongside existing holders. Do not accept uncapped pool increases after closing.
- **Board composition:** Maintain a board structure where the Chief Executive Officer appoints at least one member in addition to themselves, with one investor seat at seed, and clear rules for the independent seat.
- **Reserved matters:** Require founder consent on new share issues, option pool increases, senior debt, related-party transactions, and any sale of substantially all assets.
- **Voting agreements or dual-class:** Where appropriate under counsel’s advice, use voting agreements or dual-class to protect control through specific votes rather than relying only on economic percentage.

## How this interacts with pay decisions
- When a role requires the **upper quartile of equity**, consider selecting the **lower half of the cash quartile** for that offer so the option pool lasts and the control line is respected.
- In Athens, where cash levels are lower due to local labour markets, avoid compensating entirely with equity. Use the bonus quartiles and clear scorecards so equity grants stay within band.
- For cross-border parity, keep equity **location-agnostic** and show total on-target earnings clearly, including Greek 14-month presentation where used. This keeps fairness without unintended dilution.

## One-page control checklist before any offer or round
1. Run the quick control test with current p and e.  
2. Confirm the Chief Executive Officer’s result is at or above the stage line.  
3. If below, adjust investor percentage, pool target, or introduce voting safeguards.  
4. Check that the offer’s equity quartile and cash quartile combination does not force a pool top-up ahead of plan.  
5. Ensure board composition and reserved matters are recorded in the approval pack.  
6. File the written case for any above-band grant with the board decision.
