# Founder control plan

## Purpose
Protect the Chief Executive Officer’s control while paying senior leaders fairly and keeping the option pool healthy. Control can refer to economic ownership, voting power, or both. This plan defines what control means at Couch Heroes, sets the thresholds by stage, and explains how to test control before approving any equity grant or financing round.

## What control means in practice
- **Economic control** means the Chief Executive Officer holds more than half of the fully diluted ordinary shares.
- **Voting control** means the Chief Executive Officer can carry or block board and shareholder decisions under the company’s constitution even if economic ownership drops below half. This is achieved through board composition, reserved matters, voting agreements, or, where counsel advises it is appropriate, dual-class voting.

The studio should aim for economic control at seed. If that is not practical because of round size or pool requirements, maintain voting control with clear safeguards and target a strong economic position that trends upward as milestones are achieved.

## Control thresholds by stage
These thresholds guide both hiring grants and round design.

- **Pre-seed and seed:** Chief Executive Officer at least 50.1 percent after the transaction, or equivalent voting control with board safeguards.
- **Through Series A:** Chief Executive Officer at least 33.4 percent economic ownership, with voting control protections and participation rights in place.
- **Beyond Series A:** Maintain voting control and a credible path to strengthen economic ownership through growth, selective buybacks when advised, or smaller pool refreshes after hiring peaks.

## The quick control check to run before any decision
Before approving an equity grant or term sheet, estimate the Chief Executive Officer’s percentage after the planned change. Take the Chief Executive Officer’s current fully diluted percentage and multiply it by the portion of the company that will remain after investors and the option pool are accounted for.

Put simply:  
- Start with the Chief Executive Officer’s current percentage.  
- Subtract the investor’s planned post-round percentage from one hundred percent.  
- Subtract the option pool target after the round from the remainder.  
- Multiply the Chief Executive Officer’s current percentage by that final remainder.

If the result is below the control threshold for the stage, do not proceed without changes. Reduce the investor percentage, reduce the pool target, or add voting protections first.

## Illustrative control scenarios

### Scenario A: Control preserved at seed
- **Before the round:** Chief Executive Officer 70 percent, Chief Operating Officer 15 percent, angels 5 percent, option pool 10 percent.  
- **Planned round:** Investor to hold 15 percent after the round; option pool to be 10 percent after the round.  
- **Estimate:** The portion remaining after investor and pool is 75 percent. Seventy percent multiplied by 75 percent equals 52.5 percent.  
- **Outcome:** Economic control is preserved. Record board composition and reserved matters to ensure voting control also holds.

### Scenario B: Control lost without safeguards
- **Before the round:** Chief Executive Officer 60 percent, Chief Operating Officer 15 percent, angels 15 percent, option pool 10 percent.  
- **Planned round:** Investor to hold 20 percent after the round; option pool to be 15 percent after the round.  
- **Estimate:** The portion remaining after investor and pool is 65 percent. Sixty percent multiplied by 65 percent equals 39.0 percent.  
- **Outcome:** Economic control would be lost. To proceed safely, reduce the investor percentage, reduce the pool target, or put voting control protections in place before signing.

### Scenario C: Voting control used where economics dip
- **Before the round:** Chief Executive Officer 58 percent, others 27 percent, option pool 15 percent.  
- **Planned round:** Investor to hold 22 percent after the round; option pool remains 15 percent after the round.  
- **Estimate:** The portion remaining after investor and pool is 63 percent. Fifty-eight percent multiplied by 63 percent equals 36.5 percent.  
- **Outcome:** Economic control dips below fifty percent. Proceed only with confirmed voting protections: a board majority or equivalent, reserved matters covering new share issues, option pool increases, senior debt, related-party transactions, and any sale of substantially all assets, plus founder participation rights. Record these protections before issuing a term sheet.

## Equity and grant policy that supports control
- **Location neutrality:** Equity grants are the same for London and Athens at the same level so ownership remains fair and transparent.  
- **Grant bands:** Use the equity quartiles defined in the guide. Remain within band unless a short written case proves role criticality and scarcity.  
- **Option pool sizing:** Begin at ten percent fully diluted at seed. Refresh only against signed hiring plans. Keep the pool between ten and twelve percent between rounds. Do not agree to automatic refreshes unless the plan requires it.  
- **Above-band grants:** Require a written case that explains scarcity, business value, control impact, and whether the option pool remains sufficient. Attach the case to the board approval.  
- **Founder recognition:** Avoid new founder equity grants after formation. Recognise founder capital through loans, fees, or similar instruments rather than repeated equity awards.

## Round design and board safeguards
- **Pre-money pool negotiation:** If the pool must increase, set it before the round so that new investors dilute alongside existing holders. Avoid uncapped pool increases after closing.  
- **Board composition:** Maintain a board structure where the Chief Executive Officer appoints at least one member in addition to themselves, with a single investor seat at seed and clear rules for the independent seat.  
- **Reserved matters:** Require founder consent for new share issues, option pool increases, senior debt, related-party transactions, and any sale of substantially all assets.  
- **Voting agreements or dual-class:** Where counsel advises it is appropriate, use voting agreements or dual-class structures to protect control on key decisions rather than relying only on economic percentage.

## How control interacts with pay
- When a role needs the **upper quartile of equity**, consider selecting the **lower half of the matching cash quartile** to preserve the option pool and avoid premature pool refresh.  
- In Athens, where market cash levels are lower, do not compensate entirely with equity. Use the bonus quartiles with clear, role-specific scorecards so equity grants stay within band.  
- For cross-border fairness, keep equity location-agnostic and present total On-Target Earnings clearly, including the Greek 14-month presentation where used. This keeps fairness without pushing dilution onto the Chief Executive Officer.

## Control checklist before any grant or round
1. Estimate the Chief Executive Officer’s post-transaction percentage using the simple remainder method described above.  
2. Confirm the result meets the stage threshold.  
3. If it does not, adjust investor percentage, option pool target, or record voting protections before proceeding.  
4. Check that the equity and cash mix for the offer does not trigger an early option-pool top-up.  
5. Confirm board composition and reserved matters in the approval pack.  
6. File the written case for any grant above band with the board decision.

# Couch Heroes Leadership Compensation Guide 2025

## Executive summary
This guide explains how the leadership of Couch Heroes will determine executive compensation in London and Athens for Chief, Vice-President, and Director roles in an AA, pre-revenue studio with AAA ambition. The approach balances three elements. First, the scope and accountability of each role. Second, the cost of labour by location. Third, demonstrated capability and time in the seat. Base pay, annual bonus, and equity are expressed in quartiles so the team can recognise strength without breaking internal parity. London and Athens are treated fairly by anchoring cash to location and keeping equity location-agnostic. Currency is shown in the local contract currency with the alternate in parentheses for clarity. Greek fourteen-month pay practice is explained so offers are unambiguous.

## 1. How decisions are made
Compensation decisions combine role, location, and demonstrated skill. Begin with the correct city table. For London, base salary quartiles are shown in pounds with euros in parentheses. For Athens, base salary quartiles are shown in euros with pounds in parentheses. Select a quartile that reflects demonstrated capability and time in role, not just job title. A first-time leader in the seat belongs in the lower half of the chosen quartile, an experienced operator belongs near the middle, and a scale veteran with multiple shipped titles or function build-outs belongs in the upper half. Record a brief rationale for each placement so the decision remains clear at board review.

Quartiles provide structured headroom to recognise skill and scope without breaking internal parity. To avoid pay inversion, the Chief Executive Officer quartiles sit above the highest functional medians appropriate to an AA studio. Annual bonus targets and equity grants use matching quartiles. This keeps the overall package coherent and avoids over-reliance on any single element.

## 2. Placement matrix for capability and time in role
Use the matrix below as the first filter. It guides where an individual should sit before any fine adjustments for scope or market scarcity.

| Capability | 0 to 12 months | 12 to 36 months | 36 months plus |
|---|---|---|---|
| Foundational | Quartile 1 to the lower half of Quartile 2 | Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 | Quartile 2 |
| Proficient | Quartile 2 | Mid to upper Quartile 2 | Lower Quartile 3 |
| Expert | Quartile 2 to lower Quartile 3 | Quartile 3 | Upper Quartile 3 to Quartile 4 |

## 3. Base salary tables

## 4. Annual bonus design
Annual bonus targets are expressed as a percentage of base salary and are aligned across locations so incentives remain consistent. Each role has a short, weighted scorecard tied to measurable outcomes. Bonus payout equals the target percentage multiplied by the weighted score for the agreed Key Performance Indicators. The weights are disclosed in the offer letter so there is no ambiguity at year end.

| Role | Quartile 1 | Quartile 2 | Quartile 3 | Quartile 4 |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Chief Executive Officer | 10% to 20% | 20% to 30% | 30% to 35% | 35% to 40% |
| Chief Operating Officer | 10% to 15% | 15% to 20% | 20% to 25% | 25% to 30% |
| Chief Financial Officer | 10% to 15% | 15% to 20% | 20% to 25% | 25% to 30% |
| Chief Technology Officer | 10% to 15% | 15% to 20% | 20% to 25% | 25% to 30% |
| Chief Product Officer | 10% to 15% | 15% to 20% | 20% to 25% | 25% to 30% |
| Executive Producer | 10% to 12% | 12% to 14% | 14% to 15% | 15% to 18% |

Design intent varies by role. For the Chief Executive Officer, heavier weight sits on funding or revenue gates, on-time delivery of key milestones, leadership hiring and team health, and reporting quality and timeliness. For the Chief Operating Officer, readiness and throughput dominate. For the Chief Financial Officer, cash runway, audit quality, and forecast accuracy are central. Chief Technology Officer, Chief Product Officer, and Executive Producer scorecards follow the same principle, aligned to outcomes they directly influence.

## 5. Equity grant bands
Equity is expressed as a fully diluted percentage at grant. Vesting is four years with a one-year cliff. Equity is location-agnostic so that leaders in London and Athens are treated fairly on ownership. The table shows where typical grants should land by quartile.

| Role | Quartile 1 | Quartile 2 | Quartile 3 | Quartile 4 |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Chief Executive Officer | 2.00% to 2.75% | 2.75% to 3.50% | 3.50% to 4.25% | 4.25% to 5.00% |
| Chief Operating Officer | 0.25% to 0.45% | 0.45% to 0.65% | 0.65% to 0.85% | 0.85% to 1.00% |
| Chief Financial Officer | 0.25% to 0.45% | 0.45% to 0.65% | 0.65% to 0.85% | 0.85% to 1.00% |
| Chief Technology Officer | 0.25% to 0.45% | 0.45% to 0.65% | 0.65% to 0.85% | 0.85% to 1.00% |
| Chief Product Officer | 0.25% to 0.45% | 0.45% to 0.65% | 0.65% to 0.85% | 0.85% to 1.00% |
| Executive Producer | 0.10% to 0.15% | 0.15% to 0.20% | 0.20% to 0.25% | 0.25% to 0.30% |

Governance rules are as follows. Any grant above band requires a short written case that explains scarcity, business value, effect on founder control, and whether the option pool remains sufficient. The option pool should begin around ten percent at seed and rise only when a signed hiring plan requires it. Pool increases should be negotiated pre-money so all holders dilute in proportion.

## 6. Cross-border consistency and Greek fourteen-month practice
Fairness across London and Athens depends on comparing like with like. London operates on a twelve-month payroll. Greece often presents pay over fourteen months in the private sector, with one extra month at Christmas and two half-months at Easter and holiday. Offers in Athens must be quoted as annualised figures and must state whether those allowances are included in the annualised base or paid as separate instalments. Maintain parity by equalising annual On-Target Earnings rather than the monthly cheque. For example, an annualised base of €180,000 pays €12,857 per month on a fourteen-month pattern or €15,000 per month on a twelve-month pattern. The yearly total is the same. The contract must specify the method and the monthly presentation shown to the employee should match it.

## 7. Operating safeguards
Several checks keep decisions fair and affordable. A peer parity check prevents unjustified gaps for the same role and quartile in the same city. A non-inversion check ensures the Chief Executive Officer remains above the highest functional median in that city. A budget check confirms that combined base pay and target bonuses for the leadership team fit inside the agreed share of operating costs. A founder control test confirms that planned grants and any option pool refresh do not push the Chief Executive Officer below the target ownership threshold for the stage. Finally, the currency rule requires that offers are issued and paid in the local currency of contract, with the alternate currency shown in parentheses for internal comparison only.

Before the round, the Chief Executive Officer holds 70 percent, the Chief Operating Officer holds 15 percent, angels hold 5 percent, and the option pool is 10 percent. The planned round gives the investor 15 percent after the round and sets the option pool at 10 percent after the round. The portion remaining after investor and pool is 75 percent. Seventy percent multiplied by 75 percent equals 52.5 percent. Economic control is preserved. Record board composition and reserved matters to ensure voting control also holds.

Scenario B, control lost without safeguards. Before the round, the Chief Executive Officer holds 60 percent, the Chief Operating Officer holds 15 percent, angels hold 15 percent, and the option pool is 10 percent. The planned round gives the investor 20 percent after the round and sets the option pool at 15 percent after the round. The portion remaining after investor and pool is 65 percent. Sixty percent multiplied by 65 percent equals 39.0 percent. Economic control would be lost. To proceed safely, reduce the investor percentage, reduce the pool target, or put voting control protections in place before signing.

Scenario C, voting control used where economics dip. Before the round, the Chief Executive Officer holds 58 percent, others hold 27 percent, and the option pool is 15 percent. The planned round gives the investor 22 percent after the round and keeps the option pool at 15 percent. The portion remaining after investor and pool is 63 percent. Fifty-eight percent multiplied by 63 percent equals 36.5 percent. Economic control dips below fifty percent. Proceed only with confirmed voting protections: a board majority or equivalent, reserved matters covering new share issues, option-pool increases, senior debt, related-party transactions, and any sale of substantially all assets, plus founder participation rights. Record these protections before issuing a term sheet.

**Equity and grant policy that supports control.**  
Equity grants are the same for London and Athens at the same level so ownership remains fair and transparent. Use the equity quartiles defined in this guide and remain within band unless a short written case proves role criticality and market scarcity. Begin with an option pool of about ten percent fully diluted at seed. Refresh only against signed hiring plans. Keep the pool between ten and twelve percent between rounds. Do not agree to automatic refreshes unless the plan requires it. Any grant above band requires a written case that explains scarcity, business value, control impact, and whether the option pool remains sufficient. Attach the case to the board approval. Avoid new founder equity grants after formation. Recognise founder capital through loans, fees, or similar instruments rather than repeated equity awards.

**Round design and board safeguards.**  
If the option pool must increase, set it before the round so that new investors dilute alongside existing holders. Avoid uncapped pool increases after closing. Maintain a board structure where the Chief Executive Officer appoints at least one member in addition to themselves, with a single investor seat at seed and clear rules for the independent seat. Require founder consent for new share issues, option-pool increases, senior debt, related-party transactions, and any sale of substantially all assets. Where counsel advises it is appropriate, use voting agreements or dual-class structures to protect control on key decisions rather than relying only on economic percentage.

**How control interacts with pay.**  
When a role needs the upper quartile of equity, consider selecting the lower half of the matching cash quartile to preserve the option pool and avoid premature pool refresh. In Athens, where market cash levels are lower, do not compensate entirely with equity. Use the bonus quartiles with clear, role-specific scorecards so equity grants stay within band. For cross-border fairness, keep equity location-agnostic and present total On-Target Earnings clearly, including the Greek fourteen-month presentation where used. This keeps fairness without pushing dilution onto the Chief Executive Officer.

**Control checklist before any grant or round.**  
Estimate the Chief Executive Officer’s post-transaction percentage using the simple remainder method described above. Confirm the result meets the stage threshold. If it does not, adjust investor percentage, option-pool target, or record voting protections before proceeding. Check that the equity and cash mix for the offer does not trigger an early option-pool top-up. Confirm board composition and reserved matters in the approval pack. File the written case for any grant above band with the board decision.

## 9. Evidence and refresh
Maintain a concise evidence table alongside this guide. For each role and city, note the named source, the date it was captured, whether the line is directly observed or a proxy, a confidence tag, and the next refresh date. London should be reconfirmed annually. Athens should be reconfirmed on the same cadence or at a financing event that changes the plan. The Athens Chief Product Officer line is the current priority for refresh when reliable games-specific data become available.

## 10. Closing note
This guide is intended as a practical reference for the leadership of Couch Heroes. It sets clear ranges and steps so compensation decisions can be made quickly, explained clearly, and kept consistent across London and Athens. Where a justified exception is needed, document the reasoning and attach the relevant evidence so the choice remains transparent over time.

You’re right. The COO equity bands in the table are for non-founder hires. A COO who already holds 5 percent is in the founder lane and should not be compared to the hire bands.

Here is how to handle it cleanly, without weakening CEO control.

# What to do with a COO at 5 percent

## 1) Treat the COO as founder class
- Record 5 percent as founder equity. Do not “top up” just to match the hire table. The hire bands exist for new executives who join without founder stakes.

## 2) Align vesting and retention without inflating ownership
Pick one of these, depending on your goals:

- **Keep 5 percent, no new equity.** Use cash and bonus inside the Athens COO Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 ranges you selected. This is the default and simplest path.
- **Retention overlay, not a top-up.** If you need extra stickiness, grant a small option refresh of 0.25 to 0.50 percent with four-year vesting and a one-year cliff, tied to delivery milestones. Keep the grant inside the control line tests below.
- **Re-vesting by agreement.** If the 5 percent is fully vested and you want stronger forward alignment, you can agree to re-vest a portion of the founder stake over four years. Get legal and tax advice first.

## 3) Plan for round dilution so there are no surprises
Before any equity decision or financing, estimate post-round percentages using the remainder method in plain steps:

- Start with the COO’s current fully diluted percentage. Here that is 5 percent.
- Subtract the investor’s planned post-round percentage from one hundred percent.
- Subtract the post-round option pool target from the remainder.
- Multiply 5 percent by that final remainder. The result is the COO’s estimated post-round percentage.

Example for illustration only: if investors will hold 20 percent after the round and the option pool target after the round is 12 percent, the remainder is 68 percent. Five percent multiplied by 68 percent equals 3.4 percent. If your internal retention floor for a founder-COO through Series A is, for example, 3 to 4 percent, you can set a contingent option that vests only at close to bring the COO back to the floor, subject to the CEO control test.

## 4) Keep equity location-agnostic and balance with cash
Equity does not change because the COO is in Athens. Location differences show up in cash and bonus, not ownership. Since the COO already holds founder-level equity, keep cash within the Athens COO Quartile 1 to Quartile 2 base and bonus targets, and do not try to “make up” cash with more equity.

## 5) Run the CEO control checks each time
- Confirm the CEO remains at or above the control threshold for the stage after any grant or round.
- If a retention top-up for the COO would push the CEO below the threshold, reduce the grant, adjust cash, or add voting safeguards instead.

# Suggested addition to the white paper

**Founder incumbents.** Equity bands shown in this guide apply to non-founder hires. Where a senior leader already holds a founder-level stake, treat that stake as the equity component of their package. Use cash and bonus within the appropriate quartile for role and location. Any additional equity requires a short written case, must pass the control tests, and should prefer small, milestone-based refresh grants rather than large, permanent increases.

# Couch Heroes Leadership Compensation Guide 2025  
UK and Greece

## Executive summary
This guide sets defensible compensation quartiles for Chief, Vice-President, and Director roles across the UK and Greece for an AA, pre-revenue studio with AAA ambition. It balances role scope, location labour markets, and demonstrated capability and tenure, and integrates annual bonus and equity guidance that preserves founder control. Chief Technology Officer and Chief Product Officer focus on delivery, quality, and player outcomes; Executive Producer on milestone delivery and live-ops readiness.

### Founder control plan
Purpose. Protect Chief Executive Officer control while paying leaders fairly and preserving the option pool.

What control means. Economic control is more than half of fully diluted ordinary shares. Voting control is the ability to carry or block board and shareholder decisions under the constitution, even if economic ownership dips below half, achieved using board composition, reserved matters, voting agreements, or dual-class where counsel advises it is appropriate.

Stage thresholds.  
Pre-seed and seed: at least 50.1 percent post-transaction, or equivalent voting control with board safeguards.  
Through Series A: at least 33.4 percent economic ownership with voting control protections in place. You currently exceed this threshold.  
Beyond Series A: maintain voting control and a path to strengthen economic ownership through growth and prudent pool refresh.

Quick control check before any decision. Estimate the Chief Executive Officer’s post-transaction percentage by multiplying the current percentage by the remainder after planned investor stake and the option-pool target. If the result falls below the stage threshold, reduce investor percentage, reduce the pool target, or add voting protections before proceeding.

Round design and board safeguards. Increase the option pool pre-money when needed so all holders dilute proportionally; avoid uncapped post-closing pool increases. Keep a board structure that preserves a founder-aligned majority and reserve matters for new share issues, option-pool increases, senior debt, related-party transactions, and any sale of substantially all assets.

How equity interacts with cash. If a role requires the upper equity quartile, consider the lower half of the matching cash quartile to avoid premature pool refresh. Keep equity location-agnostic so fairness is not achieved by transferring dilution onto the founder.

## 6. Cross-border practice: UK and Greece
Equity is location-agnostic across UK and Greece. Cash is location-specific. For Greece, offers must specify whether Christmas, Easter, and vacation allowances are included in the annualised base or paid as separate instalments. Present annualised On-Target Earnings so UK and Greece packages compare like-for-like. Greek practice commonly presents as fourteen months; UK presents as twelve months. Both must add to the same annual figure when compared. citeturn0search18turn0search14

- The guide now works by location first, then capability and tenure, then role quartiles. This mirrors how real offers are built and avoids back-and-forth page flipping.

- Tables are short enough to choose a number quickly, but not so narrow that managers are forced to over-use exceptions.

- Governance checks are spelled out so exceptions are visible and traceable.

## Comparison to typical market guides
- Many generic salary guides present UK-only ranges without explicit equity or founder-control mechanics. This document goes further by integrating control, option-pool policy, and Greece-specific payroll practice, which are usually omitted.  
- Compared to recruiter brochures that quote a single number, these quartiles create room to recognise capability and scarcity without losing internal parity.  
- The explicit refresh plan and evidence trail are stronger than most public guides.

1. Commission a targeted Greece games leadership pulse once hiring starts to replace producer and product proxies with direct data.

# VP and Director Compensation Bands (UK and Greece)

- **Quartiles**: Quartile 1 is the lower market quartile, Quartile 4 the upper market quartile. Use Quartile 2–3 for standard hiring, Quartile 4 for scarce or exceptional talent.
- **Base currency and parentheses**: UK bands are shown in pounds with euros in parentheses. Greece bands are shown in euros with pounds in parentheses.  
  FX basis used for conversions: **1 GBP ≈ 1.145 EUR** and **1 EUR ≈ 0.872 GBP** on 27 Oct 2025, ECB reference. citeturn5search4
- **Stage and context**: These are pre-revenue AA studio targets. Budget to Quartile 2 for most hires initially, with bonus and equity at mid-targets unless the role is a critical path leader.

## Notes on differentials and fairness
- For like-for-like roles, expect Greece director-level cash to run at roughly 50–70 percent of London for engineering and creative leadership, based on ERI London vs Athens leadership comps and UK games anchors. Adjust toward the higher end if the role is export-facing or requires daily English-language stakeholder work. citeturn3search13turn2search6
- Keep **bonus and equity** targets aligned across locations to avoid perceived structural disadvantage. If cash differs by location, equity is the fairest normaliser given similar scope and impact. Equity benchmarks in Europe did not expand materially in 2025, so avoid over-promising. citeturn6search15

# Worksheet: Offer Design and Approval (copy into Excel)

Paste these headers in row 1, then one row per candidate. The formulas assume a FX cell where you maintain the live rate.

**Columns**
Role | Level (VP or Director) | Function | Location (UK or Greece) | Capability Tier (Foundational, Proficient, Advanced) | Selected Quartile (1–4) | Base Currency | Base Amount | Alt Currency | Alt Amount | Target Bonus % | Target Equity % | Sign-on Allowance | Relocation Allowance | Notes | Approver | Offer Status

**Set-up cells**
- Cell **B2**: FX_GBP_to_EUR = **1.145**.  
- Cell **B3**: FX_EUR_to_GBP = **0.872**.  Source: ECB reference, 27 Oct 2025. citeturn5search4

**Formulas**
- If **Base Currency** = GBP, then **Alt Currency** = EUR and **Alt Amount** = `Base Amount * FX_GBP_to_EUR`.  
- If **Base Currency** = EUR, then **Alt Currency** = GBP and **Alt Amount** = `Base Amount * FX_EUR_to_GBP`.  
- For **Target Bonus %** and **Target Equity %**, use the mid-points in the band above unless you have a written exception for scarce hire or critical path delivery.

**Decision checks**
- Does the selected quartile match interview outcome against capability tier and scope of role  
- Is the bonus tied to measurable goals the VP/Director can control  
- Is equity consistent with peers at the same level across locations  
- Has Legal confirmed that vesting, cliff, and acceleration terms match the studio’s plan  
- Has Finance validated the budget impact across 12 and 24 months

---

## Evidence and sources
- UK games titles and director-level anchors for Production, Design, Art, Studio leadership, 2025 updates. citeturn1view0  
- 2025 gaming salary review release for broader trend confirmation. citeturn1view1  
- London Director of Engineering and range benchmarks, 2025. citeturn3search13turn3search10  
- London VP Engineering and VP Product reference ranges, 2025. citeturn4search1turn4search3turn4search2  
- Greece engineering leadership medians and Athens senior engineering director anchor. citeturn2search12turn2search6  
- Greece Director of Product and Marketing Director medians. citeturn2search7turn2search3  
- Greece wage pressure and context in 2025. citeturn2news53  
- Startup salary and equity trend signals used to set conservative VP and Director equity targets in Europe, 2024–2025. citeturn6search15turn6search18  
- FX reference rate used for parentheses conversions. citeturn5search4

---

## Quick usage guide
1) Choose the role and location. Pick the **Selected Quartile** based on interview evidence against **Capability Tier** and business scarcity.  
2) Set **Base Amount** within the quartile. The **Alt Amount** converts automatically.  
3) Apply **Target Bonus %** from the role band. Tie to 3–5 measurable KPIs.  
4) Set **Target Equity %** per band and align vesting with the studio-wide plan.  
5) Log notes and route for CFO approval before issuing a formal offer.

# Annual bonus targets
Set bonus targets consistently by role and by location. Use company performance and role KPIs. Even at pre-revenue, define a capped structure so you are not renegotiating every quarter.

- CEO: 0–20% target. Pay only on milestone delivery and cash runway gates. Seed to Series A founder data supports modest base plus performance-linked upside. citeturn6search4  
- COO, CTO, CFO, CPO: 10–25% target at UK bands, 8–20% target in Greece.  
- VP layer: 8–15% UK, 5–12% Greece.  
- Director layer: 5–10% UK, 3–8% Greece.

---

# Equity guidance that preserves founder control
Given CEO already holds 51%+ and COO holds 5%, keep additional C-suite grants tight and vesting standard.

- CEO: no new primary grant. Future refresh only if required by Series B investors.  
- COO: existing 5% respected; any refresh as performance-based top-ups, not new primary.  
- CTO: 0.5–1.5% new hire or refresh equivalent at Series A stage, four-year vest with one-year cliff, double-trigger protection only.  
- CFO, CPO: 0.25–1.0% each.  
- VP layer: 0.10–0.40%.  
- Director layer: 0.05–0.20%.  
These ranges keep cumulative dilution modest and are consistent with European startup practice while recognising games industry risk premium. citeturn6search4

---

# Quick placement rules that stop overpaying
1) Start with role and quartile, then adjust one notch for London vs Greece.  
2) Adjust one notch for a proven multi-platform or live-service ship in the last four years.  
3) Do not stack adjustments more than two notches without board approval.  
4) Bonus only trips at studio-level gates: cash runway ≥ 12 months after payment, green-lit milestone achieved, and post-mortem KPIs met.  
5) Equity is for leverage and retention. Keep cash honest, keep grants scarce, and use refreshers in place of new primaries.

---

# Why these levels are credible
- The UK executive anchors reflect 2025 London ranges reported by Robert Half and Morgan McKinley. We downshifted to AA pre-revenue reality rather than FTSE-scale or late-stage tech figures. citeturn8search0turn8search2  
- Games leadership (Director, VP, studio production) aligns with 2024/25 Skillsearch and other 2025 UK gaming salary snapshots, which sit materially below big-tech executive medians. citeturn6search5turn7search7  
- Greece bands use ERI/SalaryExpert national data to define an upper envelope, then we select quartiles appropriate for an AA studio, which is why they sit below the national executive medians for some roles. citeturn10search12turn10search9  
- Currency conversions use the current October 2025 EUR→GBP average around 0.869. citeturn12search0

# What to do next if any number still feels high
- Place each current leader into a quartile with a one-line justification.  
- Cross-check against the cited sources for the closest comparable role.  
- If you need to trim further for runway, drop one quartile tier and compensate with a modest equity refresh and a performance bonus that only pays when the cash runway tests pass.

[USER]
Can they realistically hire someone who is at expert in quirtile 1 or 2?

[ASSISTANT]
Short answer: a true expert almost never accepts Quartile 1, and only sometimes accepts Quartile 2. It can work, but only if the non-cash levers are strong and the offer is structured to step up quickly on delivery. Feasibility also differs by location.

# What “expert in Quartile 1 or 2” really means
- **Expert** here = shipped multiple titles or platforms, built or run a function at scale, repeatable delivery, strong references.
- **Quartile 1** = bottom of credible market for the role and location.  
- **Quartile 2** = lower-mid market for the role and location.

# Reality by location
- **UK:** Hiring a genuine expert at Quartile 1 is not realistic. Quartile 2 can work only if you offer outsized non-cash value and fast, automatic progression to the upper quartiles on milestone delivery.  
- **Greece:** More plausible than the UK, but still uncommon for true experts. Quartile 2 is attainable with the right mix of equity, scope, and flexibility. Quartile 1 will usually under-clear unless scope is narrower than typical for the title.

# When Quartile 2 can succeed
You need at least three of these levers to be compelling.
1. **Equity at the upper end of the band** with clear upside and standard four-year vest, plus double-trigger protection.  
2. **Scope and creative control** that the candidate cannot get elsewhere, documented in the JD and OKRs.  
3. **Fast, automatic pay step-ups** tied to objective milestones, not manager discretion.  
4. **Mission, founder quality, and visibility** that improve the candidate’s career narrative.  
5. **Flexibility** on location, remote pattern, or a four-day schedule without career penalty.  
6. **Sign-on to replace forfeited bonus or equity** at their current employer.  
7. **Clear runway gates** so bonuses pay only when safe, but do pay when earned.

# When it fails
- Competing with late-stage studios or big tech on the same candidate.  
- Vague equity or unclear option-pool headroom.  
- No documented step-up path.  
- Mislabelled scope where the “expert” is actually carrying VP or C-level responsibility at a Director title and Quartile 2 pay.

# Recommended offer patterns

## UK example
- **Base:** Quartile 2 midpoint for the role.  
- **Bonus:** At or slightly above Quartile 2 target with a short, measurable scorecard.  
- **Equity:** Upper Quartile 3 to Quartile 4 of the equity band, location-agnostic.  
- **Step-ups:** Automatic move to the next cash quartile after two delivered gates, for example “vertical slice accepted” and “first platform certification passed,” with effective dates and amounts written into the offer.  
- **Sign-on:** One-time, capped, used only to cover forfeitures.

## Greece example
- **Base:** Quartile 2 midpoint annualised, with Greek allowances clarified in the contract.  
- **Bonus:** 12–15 percent target, paid only when the runway gate is met.  
- **Equity:** Mid to upper band for the level to normalise location gap.  
- **Step-ups:** Same milestone logic as the UK.

# Guardrails to protect parity and control
- Do not place a true expert below Quartile 2 on cash. If you must, increase equity and write fast step-ups.  
- Keep equity within the published band and check the founder-control test before approving.  
- Document a one-line rationale for the quartile placement and the milestone triggers.

# Decision checklist for the hire
1. Is the candidate a proven expert by your definition, or a strong Proficient?  
2. Can you offer three or more of the levers listed above?  
3. Are step-ups automatic, dated, and tied to objective deliverables?  
4. Does the package pass the peer-parity, budget, and founder-control checks?  
5. Would you be comfortable if this exact offer leaked internally?

**Bottom line:**  
- **Quartile 1 for a real expert:** not realistic in either market.  
- **Quartile 2 for a real expert:** sometimes, if equity, scope, and progression are strong and unambiguous.  
- **Best practice:** start at Quartile 2 with upper-band equity and pre-written step-ups to Quartile 3 on delivery.
